العطار
على
تقبلُ القِسمةَ واللَّاقِسمةَ باعتبار وجودِها الذهني بالكيف باعتبار وجوده الخارجي، وأنَّ العِلْمَ مِنَ الأمور الاعتباريَّةِ، ويردُّ عليهِ : أنَّه لو كانَ مُرادُهُم بكونِهِ مِن مقولة الكَيْفِ كونَهُ مُشابِها لِلكَيف ؛ لم يكن وجه لاستدلالهم على أنَّهُ مِن مقولة الكيفِ لَا من مقولة الانفعالِ والإضافة؛ إذْ يجوز أن يكون إضافةً وانفعالاً شبيهاً بالكيف، ولم يكن نزاع المخالفين في ذلك حقيقيًّا بَل لفظيا، وقال بعضُ آخَرُ : إِنَّهُ لا مانع مِن كونِ الشَّيء جوهراً في الخارج وعَرَضاً في الذهن، ونُوقِش بأَنَّ العَرَضَ ماهيَّةٌ، إذا وجِدَت في الخارج ؛ كانت في موضوع ، وهَهُنا ليس كذلك، فالحقُّ ما أفاده العلامة زاهد مِن أنَّ لِلعِلْمِ مَعنَيين ؛ الأوَّل : المعنى المصدري ، والثَّاني : المعنى الذهني الَّذِي بِهِ الانكشاف، والأوَّلُ هو حصولُ الصُّورةِ والثَّاني هو الصُّورةُ الحَاصِلَةُ، ولا شَكٍّ أنَّ الغرضَ العِلمي لا يتعلَّق بالأَوَّلِ ؛ فإنَّهُ ليسَ كاسباً ولا مكتسباً، فالمراد بحصولِ الصُّورةِ هَهُنا ؛ الصُّورة الحاصلة على سبيل المسامحة، هذا ما يذهب إليه النَّظرُ الجلي، ثمَّ النَّظرُ الدَّقيقُ يحكم بأنَّ المراد بحصولِ الصُّورةِ المعنى الحاصِلُ بالمصدر، وهي حالة إدراكيَّةٌ تَتَحَقَّقُ عند حصولِ الشَّيء في الذهن، وتلك الحالةُ الإدراكية تصدقُ على الأشياء الحاصِلَةِ بالذهن صدقاً عرضيّا، وذلكَ لأَنَّهُ إذا حصل شيءٌ في الذهن؛ يحصل له وصف يحمل ذلك الوصف عليه؛ فيقال له صورة
Introduction of the author (al-matn). al-Dasuqi: 'Its comprehension.' Then indeed knowledge in the sense of perception was said: it is from the category of quality, and it is an accident that does not depend on the comprehension of something else, and does not require division and non-division in its subject, like blackness and whiteness. On this, perception is the form of a thing obtained in the mind. And it was said: it is from the category of action, which is the influence of a thing on another as long as it is influencing, like the heating of fire on water as long as it is heating. On this, perception is interpreted as obtaining the form of a thing in the mind. And it was said: from the category of passion, which is the influence of a thing from another as long as it is affected, like the heating of water from fire as long as the water is being heated. On this, perception is interpreted as the soul's acceptance of the form of a thing in it. And it was said: from the category of relation, which is a relation whose comprehension depends on the comprehension of another relation, like fatherhood and sonship, for each of them is a relation whose comprehension depends on the comprehension of the other. This is intended by 'relation' in opposition to action and passion. And what is intended by it here, in respect of knowledge, is the relation, i.e., that it is a relation between two things whose comprehension depends on the comprehension of each of them. On this, it is interpreted. al-Atar: Their statement. And the most correct of these views is the first. End. Then, upon making knowledge from the category of quality, a famous objection arises based on the fact that what is obtained in the mind is the things themselves, according to what the verifiers among the philosophers hold, not their likenesses. And likewise, according to some of them, a single essence can be from the category of substance in one respect and from the category of accident in another respect, like the imagined Zayd; for he, in respect of his external existence, is from the category of substance, and in respect of his mental existence, from the category of quality, and it is one of the nine divisions of accident. They differed in the answer. Mulla Sadra al-Shirazi said: Things after their occurrence in the mind are transformed into the category of quality, even if the known is not a quality, based on the mind being a 'salt-pit' [that transforms what enters it]. So just as everything that falls into it becomes salt, so everything that occurs in the mind becomes a quality. There is in this that the mind being like a salt-pit is a claim without evidence, rather this is similar to rhetoric. And his contemporary Jalal al-Dawani said: There is no transformation. Accordingly, knowledge of every category is identical with that category, and that knowledge is absolutely a quality by way of simile, i.e., likening the mental form to [a quality] in that it does not... Perception is that it is the obtaining of a form of a thing in the mind. And what the verifiers are upon is that it is of the genus of quality. Accordingly, knowledge is identical in essence with the known, they only differ in consideration. The form of a thing, in respect of being imprinted in the mind, is knowledge, and in respect of its being imprinted with the thing in the external, is known. So it is not said that it is an instance of theoretical knowledge, which depends for its comprehension on the comprehension of something else, like a proof. Then the definition of quality mentioned earlier, that it is an accident whose comprehension does not depend on the comprehension of something else, would not apply to it. Because we say: what is negated is the necessity of dependence; i.e., its comprehension does not necessarily depend on the comprehension of something else. Rather, sometimes its comprehension depends on the comprehension of something else, and sometimes it does not, as mentioned by al-Sayyid al-Balidi in his commentary on the Categories. al-Atar: Upon... it accepts division and non-division in respect of its mental existence by quality in respect of its external existence, and that knowledge is among the relational matters. And it is objected to him: if what they meant by its being from the category of quality was its resembling quality, then there would be no basis for their inference that it is from the category of quality and not from the category of passion and relation, since it would be permissible for it to be a relation and passion resembling quality, and the disagreement of the opponents would not be real but verbal. And another said: There is no impediment to a thing being a substance externally and an accident in the mind. And it was objected: an accident is a quiddity that, if it exists externally, is in a subject; but here it is not so. The truth is what was stated by the scholar Zahid: that knowledge has two meanings: the first is the verbal noun meaning, and the second is the mental meaning by which disclosure occurs. The first is the obtaining of the form, and the second is the form obtained. There is no doubt that the epistemic purpose does not pertain to the first, for it is neither an acquirer nor an acquired. So what is intended by 'obtaining the form' here is the form obtained by way of leniency. This is what clear consideration leads to. Then precise consideration judges that what is intended by 'obtaining the form' is the meaning derived from the verbal noun, which is a perceptual state realized upon the occurrence of a thing in the mind. That perceptual state applies to things occurring in the mind by accidental truthfulness, because when a thing occurs in the mind, a description obtains for it, and that description is predicated of it, so it is called a form.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's definition of knowledge ('ilm). The commentator, al-Dasuqi, begins by presenting four opinions on the categorical classification of 'ilm (perception). First, it is placed in the category of quality (kayf), defined as an accident that does not depend on the comprehension of another and does not require division or non-division in its subject. On this view, perception is the form of a thing obtained in the mind. Second, it is placed in the category of action (fi'l), as an influence of one thing on another while influencing. Here, perception is the obtaining of the form in the mind. Third, it is placed in the category of passion (infi'al), as being influenced by another. Perception is then the soul's acceptance of receiving the form. Fourth, it is placed in the category of relation (idafa), which is a relation whose comprehension depends on another relation. In this view, 'ilm is a relation between two things requiring mutual comprehension. The commentator notes that the most correct (asahh) is the first, i.e., quality. Then a well-known objection arises: if the mental existent is identical to the external thing (as the philosophers hold), then how can it be a quality? This is because a single essence (like Zayd) is a substance externally but a quality mentally. The objection is that if the mental form is the thing itself, then it belongs to its own category, not necessarily quality. The commentator presents several responses. Mulla Sadra claims that things are transformed (inqilab) into quality upon entering the mind, analogizing the mind to a salt-pit that turns everything into salt. This is criticized as an unsubstantiated claim resembling rhetoric. Jalal al-Dawani denies transformation, arguing that 'ilm is always identical with its object and is called quality only by simile. Another view allows a thing to be substance externally and accident mentally, but this is objected to because an accident requires a subject in external existence, which is not the case here. The correct view, according to al-Zahid, distinguishes two meanings of 'ilm: the verbal noun (masdari) meaning the act of obtaining a form, and the mental meaning (the form itself). The epistemic purpose concerns the latter. He clarifies that 'obtaining the form' is used loosely to refer to the form obtained. Precise analysis shows that it is a perceptual state that accidentally applies to things in the mind. This resolves the apparent contradiction by showing that the definition of 'ilm as a quality is maintained while accounting for the identity of mental and external existence.

Definition of Knowledge as a Mental Form and Quality
Definition of knowledge and its classification as a quality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract the definition of knowledge from the passage, identify its genus (quality) and differentia (acquisition of form), and explain the distinction between the infinitive and mental meanings of knowledge.

Core Idea
Knowledge is the mental form of a thing, ontologically a quality, identical to the known in essence but distinct in consideration.

This passage from Tadhheeb al-Mantiq defines perception as the acquisition of a form in the mind and then classifies knowledge as belonging to the category of quality. The author addresses potential objections, clarifying that knowledge does not necessarily depend on proofs. Understanding this definition is essential for Islamic epistemology, as it distinguishes knowledge from other mental acts and grounds discussions in usul al-fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and definition
Locate where the author defines 'idrak' (perception). The definition is 'husul surah shay' fi al-dhimm' (acquisition of a form of a thing in the mind). Note that this definition is the foundation for the subsequent discussion.
The definiendum is 'idrak', but the discussion focuses on 'ilm (knowledge) as the acquired form.
2
Extract the genus and differentia
The verifiers hold that perception is of the category of quality (kayf). Thus, the genus is quality. The differentia is the specific process: acquisition of a form in the mind. Assess whether this constitutes a complete logical definition (hadd).
3
Analyze the objection and response
Read the objection: if knowledge is theoretical (dependent on a proof), it would contradict the definition of quality (which says understanding does not depend on something else). The response is that the definition negates necessity, not possibility. Sometimes knowledge depends, sometimes not.
This nuance is crucial for understanding the scope of the definition.
4
Distinguish the two meanings of knowledge
According to al-Zahid, knowledge has an infinitive meaning (the act of acquiring) and a mental meaning (the acquired form). The scientific purpose concerns the latter. Understand why the act is not the focus.
The passage uses 'husul al-surah' to refer to the acquired form by way of permission (musamaha).
5
Summarize the ontological status
Conclude that knowledge is a quality because it is an accident inhering in the mind. It is identical to the known in essence but differs by consideration: as imprinted in the mind it is knowledge, as corresponding to an external thing it is the known.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإدراك بأنه حصول صورة شيءٍ في الذهن، والذي عليه المحققون أنَّه من قبيل الكيف، وعليه؛ فالعِلْمُ عين المعلوم ذاتاً، وإنما يختلفان اعتباراً، فصورة الشَّيء باعتبار كونها مرتسمة في الذهن عِلْمٌ، وباعتبار ارتسامها بالشيء في الخارج معلوم، فَلَا يُقالُ : إِنَّهُ من أفرادِ العِلْم النظري، وهو يتوقف تعقله على تعقلِ الغَيرِ كالدليل، فَلَا يصدق عليه تعريفُ الكَيْفِ السَّابقِ مِن أَنَّهُ عَرَضُ لا يتوقَّفُ تعقُلُه تعقُلِ الغير؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : المنفي لزومُ التَّوقف ؛ أي: لا يلزم توقفُ تعقلِهِ على تعقل غيره، بلْ تارةً يتوقَّفُ تعقُلُه على تَعقُل الغير، وتارةً لا يتوقف، كما ذكر ذلكَ السَّيِّدُ البليدي في شرح المقولات . تقبلُ القِسمةَ واللَّاقِسمةَ باعتبار وجودِها الذهني بالكيف باعتبار وجوده الخارجي، وأنَّ العِلْمَ مِنَ الأمور الاعتباريَّةِ، ويردُّ عليهِ : أنَّه لو كانَ مُرادُهُم بكونِهِ مِن مقولة الكَيْفِ كونَهُ مُشابِها لِلكَيف ؛ لم يكن وجه لاستدلالهم على أنَّهُ مِن مقولة الكيفِ لَا من مقولة الانفعالِ والإضافة؛ إذْ يجوز أن يكون إضافةً وانفعالاً شبيهاً بالكيف، ولم يكن نزاع المخالفين في ذلك حقيقيًّا بَل لفظيا، وقال بعضُ آخَرُ : إِنَّهُ لا مانع مِن كونِ الشَّيء جوهراً في الخارج وعَرَضاً في الذهن، ونُوقِش بأَنَّ العَرَضَ ماهيَّةٌ، إذا وجِدَت في الخارج ؛ كانت في موضوع ، وهَهُنا ليس كذلك، فالحقُّ ما أفاده العلامة زاهد مِن أنَّ لِلعِلْمِ مَعنَيين ؛ الأوَّل : المعنى المصدري ، والثَّاني : المعنى الذهني الَّذِي بِهِ الانكشاف، والأوَّلُ هو حصولُ الصُّورةِ والثَّاني هو الصُّورةُ الحَاصِلَةُ، ولا شَكٍّ أنَّ الغرضَ العِلمي لا يتعلَّق بالأَوَّلِ ؛ فإنَّهُ ليسَ كاسباً ولا مكتسباً، فالمراد بحصولِ الصُّورةِ هَهُنا ؛ الصُّورة الحاصلة على سبيل المسامحة، هذا ما يذهب إليه النَّظرُ الجلي، ثمَّ النَّظرُ الدَّقيقُ يحكم بأنَّ المراد بحصولِ الصُّورةِ المعنى الحاصِلُ بالمصدر، وهي حالة إدراكيَّةٌ تَتَحَقَّقُ عند حصولِ الشَّيء في الذهن، وتلك الحالةُ الإدراكية تصدقُ على الأشياء الحاصِلَةِ بالذهن صدقاً عرضيّا، وذلكَ لأَنَّهُ إذا حصل شيءٌ في الذهن؛ يحصل له وصف يحمل ذلك الوصف عليه؛ فيقال له صورة
Perception is that it is the acquisition of a form of a thing in the mind, and what the verifiers hold is that it is of the category of quality. Accordingly, knowledge is identical to the known in essence, they only differ by consideration. The form of a thing, by virtue of being imprinted in the mind, is knowledge, and by virtue of its imprinting to the thing in the external world, it is known. So it is not said that it is an instance of theoretical knowledge, the understanding of which depends on understanding something else like a proof, for then the previous definition of quality—that it is an accident whose understanding does not require understanding something else—would not apply. Because we say: the negation is of the necessity of dependence; i.e., it is not necessary that its understanding depends on understanding something else. Rather, sometimes its understanding depends on understanding something else, and sometimes it does not, as mentioned by al-Sayyid al-Bulaydi in his commentary on the Categories. [It] accepts division and non-division by virtue of its mental existence as a quality by virtue of its external existence, and that knowledge is among the relational matters. It is objected to him: if their intent in considering it as a category of quality was that it resembles a quality, there would be no basis for their inference that it is from the category of quality and not from the category of passion or relation, since it is possible that it be a relation or passion resembling a quality, and the disagreement of opponents would not be real but verbal. And another said: there is no impediment to a thing being a substance externally and an accident in the mind. It is refuted by the fact that an accident is a quiddity that, if found externally, would be in a subject, but here it is not so. The truth is what the scholar Zahid conveyed, that knowledge has two meanings: first, the infinitive meaning; second, the mental meaning by which disclosure [occurs]. The first is the acquisition of the form, and the second is the form acquired. There is no doubt that the scientific purpose does not pertain to the first, for it is neither acquisitive nor acquired. So what is meant by 'acquisition of the form' here is the acquired form by way of permission. This is what evident consideration holds. Then precise consideration judges that what is meant by 'acquisition of the form' is the meaning acquired from the infinitive, which is a perceptual state that occurs when the thing is acquired in the mind. That perceptual state applies to things acquired in the mind with an accidental truth. Because when a thing is acquired in the mind, it acquires a description, and that description is predicated of it; so it is called a form.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage defines knowledge and discusses its ontological classification. The author begins by stating the common definition: perception is the acquisition of a form of a thing in the mind. The verifiers (al-muhaqqiqun) hold that this is of the category of quality (kayf). Consequently, knowledge ('ilm) is identical in essence to the known (ma'lum); they differ only in consideration (i'tibar). The form of a thing is knowledge when considered as imprinted in the mind, and it is the known when considered as corresponding to the external thing. The author addresses an objection: if knowledge is an instance of theoretical knowledge, it would require understanding a proof, which would contradict the definition of quality as an accident whose understanding does not depend on something else. The response is that the definition of quality negates the necessity of dependence, not the possibility. Sometimes knowledge does depend on something else, sometimes not, as al-Bulaydi noted. The marginal commentary by al-'Attar discusses the division of knowledge and whether it is a quality. It mentions a view that knowledge is a relational matter, and a rebuttal. The truth according to al-Zahid is that knowledge has two aspects: the infinitive (progressive) meaning, which is the act of acquiring, and the mental meaning, which is the acquired form. The scientific purpose concerns the acquired form, not the act. The precise analysis shows that 'acquisition of the form' refers to the perceptual state that arises when the thing is in the mind, and this state is accidentally predicated of the mental objects.

الصورة
الكيف
العلم
المعلوم

Key Takeaway
Knowledge is defined as the mental form of a thing, classified as a quality, and is essentially the same as the known, differing only by consideration of mental imprint vs. external existence.

The Logicians' Inclusive Definition of Tasdiq
Defines tasdiq by logicians with inclusion/exclusion conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which epistemic states logicians classify as tasdiq and which they exclude, based on the condition of certainty or opinion regarding a relation.

Core Idea
For logicians, tasdiq is any judgment of a relation with commitment, including uncertain opinion.

This lesson unpacks the logicians' definition of tasdiq as presented in the commentary. Tasdiq is a fundamental concept in logic, as it distinguishes between 'assent' and mere conceptualization. Understanding what logicians include and exclude helps grasp the scope of logical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition phrase
Find the phrase 'إِنْ كَانَ إِذْعَاناً للنِّسْبَةِ' in the text. This is the base definition of tasdiq.
The lam in 'للنسبة' is emphatic.
2
Parse the explanatory expansion
Note that al-Dasuqi explains 'إذعاناً للنسبة' as a perception (إدراك) of the relation occurring or not, with certainty (جزم) or opinion (ظن).
This perception can be certain or preponderant.
3
List the included types
The passage lists four types: opinion (ظن), compound ignorance (جهل مركب), certainty (يقين), and taqlid (تقليد). All are tasdiq because they involve judgment with some commitment.
Taqlid is certain but changeable.
4
Identify the excluded types
Doubt (شك) and illusion (وهم) are excluded because they lack certainty or opinion entirely.
The text explicitly states they are not called tasdiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتن (إِنْ كَانَ إِذْعَاناً للنِّسْبَةِ) الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : إِنْ كَانَ إِذْعَانَا لِلنِّسْبَةِ) أي : إدراكاً على وجه الجزم أو الظَّنِّ؛ أي: إنْ كانَ إدراكاً؛ لوقوعِهَا أوْ لَا وقوعِها واللَّامُ في قوله : للنّسبة؛ زائدةٌ لِلتَّقوية؛ أي: إن كان إذعان نسبة؛ أي إدراكاً لها من حيث إنَّها واقعة أو ليست بواقعة؛ سواء كانَ ذلك الإدراك راجحاً وهو الظَّنُّ، أو جازماً غير مطابق للواقع وهو الجهل، أو مُطابقاً للواقع وَلَا يقبلُ التَّغيُّرَ وهو اليقين، أو يقبلُ التَّغير بتشكيكِ مشكك، وهو التَّقليد، فكلَّ مِنَ الظَّنِّ والجهل المركَبِ واليقين والتّقليد؛ تصديق عند المناطقة؛ لإنَّهُ إدراكُ وقوع النِّسبةِ أوْ لَا وَقوعِهَا على وجه الجزم أو الظَّنِّ، وهو شامل لما ذكر، وأمَّا إدراك وقوعِهَا أوْ لَا وقوعِها على وجهِ الوهم أو الشَّكِّ؛ فَلَا يُسمَّى تصديقاً ؛ لأنَّهُ لا جزمَ وَلَا ظَنَّ عندَ الشَّاكُ والمتوهم ، وأمَّا المتكلمونَ؛ فَلَا يجعلون الظَّنَّ، والجهل، والتَّقليد ، والشَّكَّ، والوهم مِنَ العِلْمِ، بل هِيَ مُقابلةٌ له؛ لأنَّ العِلْمَ عندَهُم الاعتقاد الجازم المطابق للواقع عن دليل، والعِلْمَ عندهم غيرُ المعلوم، فالتَّصديقُ (۱) عندَهم مُقابل لِلتَّصديقِ عَندَ المناطقة؛ لأنَّ التصديق عندَ المناطقةِ مِنْ قبيل العِلْم والمعرفة، وعند المتكلمين كلام نفساني يرجعُ لقول نفْسِ المصدِّقِ : آمنْتُ وَصدَّقْتُ ؛ فَلِهذا يعرّفونَهُ بأَنَّهُ حديثُ النَّفْسِ التَّابِعُ لِلمعرفة . العطار علميَّةٌ، وهذا المحمول ليس نفْسَ الموضوع، وإلا ؛ لَكانَ محمولاً عليهِ حالَ كونِهِ في الخارج؛ ضرورة أنَّ الذات والذاتي لا يختلفان باختلاف الوجود، وهذا الحملُ مِن قبيل حمل الكاتب على الإنسان، فالعَرَضيُّ مِن مقولة الكيف؛ سواء كانَ (1) (قَوْلُهُ : فالتصديق عندهم ... إلخ) نقل العلامة الأمير في حاشيته على الجوهرة عند قول الشارح في تعريف الإيمان بأنَّه نفس المعرفة أو حديث النفس التّابع للمعرفة ما يحقق هذا المقام قال : نقل السعد عن بعض المحققين أنه أي حديث النفس قدر زائد على التصديق المنطقي لأنَّ التصديق المنطقي من أقسام العلوم فهو نفس المعرفة فعلى هذا المعاند عنده تصديق منطقي شرعي، لكنه أطال في ردّه في شرح المقاصد قائلاً : كلام ابن سينا وغيره يدلّ على أنَّ التصديق المنطقي المقابل للتصور مساو للمراد من التصديق الشَّرعي فإنَّه الحكم بمعنى الإذعان للنسبة، نعم تعقبه الخيالي بأنَّ الشَّرعيّ أخص لصدق المنطقي بالظَّن، وكذا ينفرد المنطقي في تصديق المعاند والتقليد الصحيح والفاسد . أ . هـ . ببعض تصرف . ا . هـ. الشّرنوبي.
The author's introduction: 'If it is an assent to the relation.' al-Dasuqi: His statement: 'If it is an assent to the relation' means: a perception in the mode of certainty or opinion; i.e., if it is a perception of its occurrence or non-occurrence, and the lam in 'li-al-nisba' is extra for emphasis; i.e., if it is an assent to a relation, i.e., a perception of it in terms of that it is occurring or not occurring, whether that perception is preponderant—which is opinion, or certain but not corresponding to reality—which is ignorance, or corresponding to reality and unchanging—which is certainty, or changing due to the doubt of a doubter—which is taqlid. Thus, all of opinion, compound ignorance, certainty, and taqlid are tasdiq according to the logicians, because it is a perception of the occurrence or non-occurrence of the relation in the mode of certainty or opinion, and it includes what was mentioned. As for the perception of its occurrence or non-occurrence in the mode of illusion or doubt, it is not called tasdiq because there is no certainty or opinion in the one who doubts or is in illusion. As for the theologians, they do not consider opinion, ignorance, taqlid, doubt, and illusion as knowledge; rather, they are opposed to it. Because knowledge for them is a certain belief corresponding to reality based on evidence, and knowledge for them is other than the known. So tasdiq (1) for them is opposite to tasdiq for the logicians, because tasdiq for the logicians is of the category of knowledge and cognition, while for the theologians it is a psychological speech that goes back to the statement of the soul of the one who affirms: 'I believe and I affirm.' Therefore, they define it as the speech of the soul that follows cognition. al-'Attar: scientific, and this predicate is not the subject itself; otherwise, it would be predicated of it while being external; necessarily, the essence and the essential do not differ with differing existence. This predication is of the type of predicating 'writer' of 'human,' so the accidental is of the category of quality, whether it is... (1) (His statement: 'So tasdiq for them... etc.') al-Amir in his hashiah on al-Jawharah transmitted at the statement of the commentator on the definition of faith that it is either cognition itself or the speech of the soul that follows cognition, which verifies this position. He said: al-Sa'd transmitted from some verifiers that the speech of the soul is an additional aspect over logical tasdiq because logical tasdiq is a division of the sciences, so it is cognition itself. Accordingly, the obstinate one has logical and legal tasdiq. But he elaborated in its refutation in Sharh al-Maqasid, saying: The words of Ibn Sina and others indicate that logical tasdiq, corresponding to tasawwur, is equivalent to what is meant by legal tasdiq, for it is judgment in the sense of assent to the relation. Yes, al-Khayali objected that the legal [tasdiq] is more specific because logical [tasdiq] applies to opinion, and likewise the logical is unique in the tasdiq of the obstinate and sound and corrupt taqlid. End. With some paraphrasing. End. al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage clarifies the definition of tasdiq (assent) and contrasts the logicians' and theologians' views. The author first quotes the matn: 'If it is an assent to the relation'. The commentator al-Dasuqi explains that this means a perception of the relation as occurring or not occurring, with certainty (jazm) or opinion (zann). The lam in 'li-al-nisba' is emphatic. Tasdiq includes various types: opinion (preponderant but not certain), ignorance (certain but false), certainty (true and unchangeable), and taqlid (certain but changeable by doubt). All these are considered tasdiq by logicians because they involve a judgment of occurrence or non-occurrence with some commitment. Perceptions of doubt (shakk) or illusion (wahm) are not tasdiq because they lack certainty or opinion. The theologians (mutakallimun) restrict knowledge to certainty based on evidence, so they exclude opinion, ignorance, etc. For them, tasdiq is a psychological speech (kalam nafsani) that is the soul's assertion of belief. Thus, their concept of tasdiq is opposite to the logicians'. The marginal comment by al-'Attar discusses predication, noting that the predicate is not the subject itself, and the accidental is a quality. The footnote by al-Sharnubi quotes al-Amir and others, delving into the relationship between logical tasdiq and legal (shar'i) tasdiq, with a debate on whether the latter is more specific.

Key Takeaway
For logicians, tasdiq is any perception of a relation's occurrence or non-occurrence with some degree of commitment, whether certain or opinionated.

The Theologians' Definition of Tasdiq and the Contrast
Defines tasdiq by theologians and contrasts with logicians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to contrast the theologians' definition of tasdiq as psychological speech with the logicians' definition and explain why the theologians exclude opinion, ignorance, and taqlid from knowledge.

Core Idea
For theologians, tasdiq is inner speech of affirmation, not just any judgment.

This lesson examines the theologians' distinctive definition of tasdiq as 'psychological speech' (kalam nafsani) and contrasts it with the logicians' broader definition. The passage also delves into a scholastic debate about whether logical tasdiq is equivalent to legal (shar'i) tasdiq. Understanding this contrast is key to appreciating different approaches to epistemology in Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Identify the theologians' definition
Find where the passage states that for theologians, tasdiq is 'كلام نفساني' (psychological speech) that follows cognition, corresponding to the soul saying 'I believe and I affirm'.
This is contrasted with the logicians' definition.
2
Note what theologians exclude from knowledge
The theologians do not consider opinion, ignorance, taqlid, doubt, or illusion as knowledge (علم). Knowledge for them is certain belief from evidence.
They restrict knowledge to certain and evidentially grounded beliefs.
3
Contrast the two definitions
Compare: logicians see tasdiq as a type of knowledge/cognition; theologians see it as a separate psychological act that follows cognition.
Thus, for theologians, tasdiq is not itself knowledge but a subsequent affirmation.
4
Trace the scholarly debate
Read the footnote (1) discussing al-Amir's transmission and the debate about whether logical tasdiq equals legal tasdiq, involving Ibn Sina, al-Khayali, and others.
This shows the real-world implications of the definition.

Source Text

واللَّامُ في قوله : للنّسبة؛ زائدةٌ لِلتَّقوية؛ أي: إن كان إذعان نسبة؛ أي إدراكاً لها من حيث إنَّها واقعة أو ليست بواقعة؛ سواء كانَ ذلك الإدراك راجحاً وهو الظَّنُّ، أو جازماً غير مطابق للواقع وهو الجهل، أو مُطابقاً للواقع وَلَا يقبلُ التَّغيُّرَ وهو اليقين، أو يقبلُ التَّغير بتشكيكِ مشكك، وهو التَّقليد، فكلَّ مِنَ الظَّنِّ والجهل المركَبِ واليقين والتّقليد؛ تصديق عند المناطقة؛ لإنَّهُ إدراكُ وقوع النِّسبةِ أوْ لَا وَقوعِهَا على وجه الجزم أو الظَّنِّ، وهو شامل لما ذكر، وأمَّا إدراك وقوعِهَا أوْ لَا وقوعِها على وجهِ الوهم أو الشَّكِّ؛ فَلَا يُسمَّى تصديقاً ؛ لأنَّهُ لا جزمَ وَلَا ظَنَّ عندَ الشَّاكُ والمتوهم ، وأمَّا المتكلمونَ؛ فَلَا يجعلون الظَّنَّ، والجهل، والتَّقليد ، والشَّكَّ، والوهم مِنَ العِلْمِ، بل هِيَ مُقابلةٌ له؛ لأنَّ العِلْمَ عندَهُم الاعتقاد الجازم المطابق للواقع عن دليل، والعِلْمَ عندهم غيرُ المعلوم، فالتَّصديقُ (۱) عندَهم مُقابل لِلتَّصديقِ عَندَ المناطقة؛ لأنَّ التصديق عندَ المناطقةِ مِنْ قبيل العِلْم والمعرفة، وعند المتكلمين كلام نفساني يرجعُ لقول نفْسِ المصدِّقِ : آمنْتُ وَصدَّقْتُ ؛ فَلِهذا يعرّفونَهُ بأَنَّهُ حديثُ النَّفْسِ التَّابِعُ لِلمعرفة . العطار علميَّةٌ، وهذا المحمول ليس نفْسَ الموضوع، وإلا ؛ لَكانَ محمولاً عليهِ حالَ كونِهِ في الخارج؛ ضرورة أنَّ الذات والذاتي لا يختلفان باختلاف الوجود، وهذا الحملُ مِن قبيل حمل الكاتب على الإنسان، فالعَرَضيُّ مِن مقولة الكيف؛ سواء كانَ (1) (قَوْلُهُ : فالتصديق عندهم ... إلخ) نقل العلامة الأمير في حاشيته على الجوهرة عند قول الشارح في تعريف الإيمان بأنَّه نفس المعرفة أو حديث النفس التّابع للمعرفة ما يحقق هذا المقام قال : نقل السعد عن بعض المحققين أنه أي حديث النفس قدر زائد على التصديق المنطقي لأنَّ التصديق المنطقي من أقسام العلوم فهو نفس المعرفة فعلى هذا المعاند عنده تصديق منطقي شرعي، لكنه أطال في ردّه في شرح المقاصد قائلاً : كلام ابن سينا وغيره يدلّ على أنَّ التصديق المنطقي المقابل للتصور مساو للمراد من التصديق الشَّرعي فإنَّه الحكم بمعنى الإذعان للنسبة، نعم تعقبه الخيالي بأنَّ الشَّرعيّ أخص لصدق المنطقي بالظَّن، وكذا ينفرد المنطقي في تصديق المعاند والتقليد الصحيح والفاسد . أ . هـ . ببعض تصرف . ا . هـ. الشّرنوبي.
The author's introduction: 'If it is an assent to the relation.' al-Dasuqi: His statement: 'If it is an assent to the relation' means: a perception in the mode of certainty or opinion; i.e., if it is a perception of its occurrence or non-occurrence, and the lam in 'li-al-nisba' is extra for emphasis; i.e., if it is an assent to a relation, i.e., a perception of it in terms of that it is occurring or not occurring, whether that perception is preponderant—which is opinion, or certain but not corresponding to reality—which is ignorance, or corresponding to reality and unchanging—which is certainty, or changing due to the doubt of a doubter—which is taqlid. Thus, all of opinion, compound ignorance, certainty, and taqlid are tasdiq according to the logicians, because it is a perception of the occurrence or non-occurrence of the relation in the mode of certainty or opinion, and it includes what was mentioned. As for the perception of its occurrence or non-occurrence in the mode of illusion or doubt, it is not called tasdiq because there is no certainty or opinion in the one who doubts or is in illusion. As for the theologians, they do not consider opinion, ignorance, taqlid, doubt, and illusion as knowledge; rather, they are opposed to it. Because knowledge for them is a certain belief corresponding to reality based on evidence, and knowledge for them is other than the known. So tasdiq (1) for them is opposite to tasdiq for the logicians, because tasdiq for the logicians is of the category of knowledge and cognition, while for the theologians it is a psychological speech that goes back to the statement of the soul of the one who affirms: 'I believe and I affirm.' Therefore, they define it as the speech of the soul that follows cognition. al-'Attar: scientific, and this predicate is not the subject itself; otherwise, it would be predicated of it while being external; necessarily, the essence and the essential do not differ with differing existence. This predication is of the type of predicating 'writer' of 'human,' so the accidental is of the category of quality, whether it is... (1) (His statement: 'So tasdiq for them... etc.') al-Amir in his hashiah on al-Jawharah transmitted at the statement of the commentator on the definition of faith that it is either cognition itself or the speech of the soul that follows cognition, which verifies this position. He said: al-Sa'd transmitted from some verifiers that the speech of the soul is an additional aspect over logical tasdiq because logical tasdiq is a division of the sciences, so it is cognition itself. Accordingly, the obstinate one has logical and legal tasdiq. But he elaborated in its refutation in Sharh al-Maqasid, saying: The words of Ibn Sina and others indicate that logical tasdiq, corresponding to tasawwur, is equivalent to what is meant by legal tasdiq, for it is judgment in the sense of assent to the relation. Yes, al-Khayali objected that the legal [tasdiq] is more specific because logical [tasdiq] applies to opinion, and likewise the logical is unique in the tasdiq of the obstinate and sound and corrupt taqlid. End. With some paraphrasing. End. al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage clarifies the definition of tasdiq (assent) and contrasts the logicians' and theologians' views. The author first quotes the matn: 'If it is an assent to the relation'. The commentator al-Dasuqi explains that this means a perception of the relation as occurring or not occurring, with certainty (jazm) or opinion (zann). The lam in 'li-al-nisba' is emphatic. Tasdiq includes various types: opinion (preponderant but not certain), ignorance (certain but false), certainty (true and unchangeable), and taqlid (certain but changeable by doubt). All these are considered tasdiq by logicians because they involve a judgment of occurrence or non-occurrence with some commitment. Perceptions of doubt (shakk) or illusion (wahm) are not tasdiq because they lack certainty or opinion. The theologians (mutakallimun) restrict knowledge to certainty based on evidence, so they exclude opinion, ignorance, etc. For them, tasdiq is a psychological speech (kalam nafsani) that is the soul's assertion of belief. Thus, their concept of tasdiq is opposite to the logicians'. The marginal comment by al-'Attar discusses predication, noting that the predicate is not the subject itself, and the accidental is a quality. The footnote by al-Sharnubi quotes al-Amir and others, delving into the relationship between logical tasdiq and legal (shar'i) tasdiq, with a debate on whether the latter is more specific.

Key Terms
المتكلمون
العلم
الاعتقاد الجازم
الكلام النفساني
المعرفة
التقليد
المعاند

C) Certain belief from evidence

Key Takeaway
For theologians, tasdiq is a distinct psychological act of affirmation that follows cognition, not the cognition itself.

Three Prerequisites for Judgment and Its Definition
Three prerequisites and definition of judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three conceptualizations required for a judgment to exist and explain how the definition of judgment as a specific type of perception refines earlier definitions.

Core Idea
Judgment is a perception, but not just any perception — it is the perception that a relation holds or does not hold.

This passage establishes the necessary conditions for the existence of judgment (hukm) and provides its precise definition. It begins by stating that three conceptualizations are required: the subject, the relational judgment, and the predicate. Then it defines judgment itself as the perception that the relation between subject and predicate is actual or not. This refines earlier definitions that identified judgment simply with tasdiq.

Guided Path
1
List the three prerequisites
The passage explicitly names three things that must be conceptualized for a judgment to exist: the subject (al-mahkum 'alayh), the relational judgment (al-nisba al-hukmiyya), and the predicate (al-mahkum bihi). Write them down.
2
Identify the genus of judgment
Judgment (hukm) is placed under the broader category of perception (idrak). This is its genus.
3
Find the differentia of judgment
The specific type of perception that defines judgment is: perception that the relation between subject and predicate is actual (waqi'a) or not actual (laysat bi-waqi'a). This is the differentia.
4
Understand the connection between prerequisites and definition
To perceive whether a relation is actual or not, one must first have the concepts of the subject, predicate, and the relation itself. Thus the three prerequisites are necessary for the very act of judgment.
This shows why the definition logically implies the prerequisites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكنْ يُشترط في وجوده ثلاثة تصورات : تصور المحكوم عليه . وتصور النسبة الحكمية . وتصور المحكوم به . وإنما قلنا : الإدراك على الوجه المذكور هو الحكم؛ لأن الحكم على ما ذكره القوم هو : إدراك أن النسبة واقعة، أو ليست بواقعة.
But three conceptualizations are required for its existence: conceptualization of the subject of judgment, conceptualization of the relational judgment, and conceptualization of the predicate of judgment. We only said: perception in the mentioned manner is the judgment; because judgment according to what the people mentioned is: perception that the relation is actual, or not actual.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage defines the conditions for the existence of judgment (hukm) and specifies its essence. First, it states that three conceptualizations (tasawwurat) are necessary: (1) conceptualizing the thing about which judgment is made (al-mahkum 'alayh), (2) conceptualizing the relational judgment (al-nisba al-hukmiyya), which is the connection between subject and predicate, and (3) conceptualizing the thing that is judged (al-mahkum bihi), i.e., the predicate. Then it clarifies that what is meant by 'perception in the mentioned manner' is indeed the judgment itself, because the standard definition of judgment among the scholars (al-qawm) is the perception that the relation between subject and predicate either actually exists (waqi'a) or does not exist (laysat bi-waqi'a). This definition grounds the three prerequisites: one cannot perceive the relation's actuality without first having the three concepts.

النسبة الحكمية (al-nisba al-hukmiyya)

Key Takeaway
Judgment is a perception that a relation holds or does not hold, and it requires prior conceptualization of the subject, predicate, and the relation itself.

Why Assent Requires Acquiescence: Refining the Definition of Tasdiq
Commentary explains why the author defines tasdiq as acquiescence to a proposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish tasdiq (assent) from takhyil (imagination), shakk (doubt), and wahm (conjecture) using the criterion of iqtinan (acquiescence).

Core Idea
Tasdiq is not just any perception of truth—it requires acquiescence to exclude imagination, doubt, and conjecture.

In this passage, the commentator explains why the author defines tasdiq as 'iqtinan' (acquiescence) to a proposition rather than the common phrase 'perceiving that the proposition is true or not true.' This refinement excludes mental states that involve perception but lack the submission that constitutes genuine assent. You will learn to identify these states and appreciate the precision required in logical definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common definition of tasdiq
The common definition criticized in the passage is 'perceiving that the proposition is true or not true.' This is the baseline that the author refines.
This definition is found in many earlier logic texts.
2
Understand the three excluded mental states
Takhyil (imagination) is a conception without hesitation; shakk (doubt) is a conception with hesitation; wahm (conjecture) is a supposition with a leaning. All three involve perceiving occurrence or non-occurrence, but none include acquiescence.
The passage defines these explicitly via Abu al-Fath.
3
Analyze the advantage of adding 'iqtinan'
By defining tasdiq as 'iqtinan li al-nisba', the author ensures that only perceptions accompanied by submission and firm acceptance count as assent. This excludes the three states above.
Al-Dawwani highlights this as the key advantage.
4
Evaluate the rebuttal and counter-rebuttal
Abu al-Fath argues that the common definition might still imply acquiescence through its wording. Mir Zahid counters that the wording can be understood without acquiescence, as it merely states perception of occurrence. Thus the author's definition is safer.
This shows the importance of precise wording in definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصِلُ مَا ذَكرَهُ مِن توجيه الاستحسان أمران؛ الأوَّلُ : الاختصارُ ، والثَّاني: التَّفرقةُ بينَ الإدراكَيْنِ المتعلِّقين بالنّسبة، فإِنَّهُ يتعلَّقُ بِهِمَا عِلْمانِ ؛ أحدُهُمَا تصوريٌّ، والآخَرُ تَصديقي كما سيظهرُ، وَوَجَّهَ العَلامَةُ الدَّوَّانِيُّ كلام المصنفِ بسلامةِ تَعريف التصديقِ المستفادِ منهُ عَن عدم المنع بخلاف تعريف قالَ : عدلَ القوم، عن العبارة المشهورة، وهي إدراكُ أَنَّ النِّسبةَ واقعةٌ أو لَيسَتْ بواقعة؛ لأنَّه يدخل فيها التَّخييلُ، فإنَّهُ إدراك لوقوع النسبة أو لا وقوعها، وكذا الشَّكُ والوهم؛ ضرورةً أنَّ المدرك في جانب الوهم هو الوقوع أو اللاوقوع، إلَّا أنَّ تلك الإدراكات ليست على وجهِ الإذعان والتسليم، بل على سبيل التخييل والتجويز ا.هـ. قال أبو الفتح : أراد بالتَّخييل؛ تَصرُّرَ الوقوعِ أو اللا وقوع مِن غيرِ تردُّدٍ ولا تجويز، والشَّكُ تصوُّرُهما على وجهِ التَّردُّدِ، والوهم تجويز أحدهما ظنّ الآخر، ويمكن دفع المناقشة عَن العبارة المشهورة بأنَّ المتبادر من إدراكِ أنَّ النّسبةَ واقعةٌ أو لَيسَتْ بواقعة؛ إدراكها على وجهِ الإذعان كما يشعرُ بِهِ عنوانُ أنَّ النَّسبة واقعةٌ أو ليست بواقعةٍ بِخِلَافِ قَولِهِم: وقوعُ النّسبة أو لا وقوعها .ا.هـ. وقد أشار مير زاهد لضعف هذا الجوابِ بِقولِهِ : وربَّما يُظنُّ أَنَّ التَّحْيِيلَ والشَّكَ والوهم إدراك لوقوعِ النَّسبة أو لا وقوعِها؛ لا لأنَّ النَّسبة واقعةٌ أو لَيسَتْ بِوَاقعةٍ، ولعلَّ مَنشأ هذا الظَّنِّ أخذُ معنى الإذعانِ في الثَّاني دونَ الأَوَّلِ ا.هـ.
The summary of what he mentioned concerning the justification of approval are two matters: first, brevity; second, the distinction between the two perceptions related to the proposition, for two sciences relate to them: one of them is conceptual (tasawwuri) and the other is assertive (tasdiqi) as will appear. Al-‘Allama al-Dawwani explained the author's statement by the safety of the definition of tasdiq derived from it from lack of prevention unlike the definition he said: the people altered the famous expression, which is 'perceiving that the proposition is true or not true', because imagination enters into it, for it is a perception of the occurrence of the proposition or its non-occurrence, and likewise doubt and conjecture, necessarily because the object perceived in the aspect of conjecture is occurrence or non-occurrence, except that those perceptions are not in the manner of acquiescence and submission, but rather in the manner of imagination and supposition. Abu al-Fath said: he meant by imagination: the conception of occurrence or non-occurrence without hesitation and without supposition; doubt is the conception of both in the manner of hesitation; conjecture is the supposition of one of them with the opinion of the other. And it is possible to rebut the criticism against the famous expression by saying that the immediate understanding from 'perceiving that the proposition is true or not true' is perceiving it in the manner of acquiescence, as is indicated by the title 'that the proposition is true or not true', unlike their saying: 'occurrence of the proposition or its non-occurrence'. And Mir Zahid indicated the weakness of this rebuttal by saying: perhaps it is thought that imagination, doubt, and conjecture are perceptions of the occurrence of the proposition or its non-occurrence, not because the proposition is true or not true, and perhaps the origin of this thought is taking the meaning of acquiescence in the second and not the first.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the definition of tasdiq (assent). The commentator explains the author's justification for defining tasdiq as 'iqtinan li al-nisba' (acquiescence to a proposition). He states two advantages: first, brevity; second, distinguishing between the two types of perception related to a proposition—one conceptual (tasawwuri) and one assertive (tasdiqi). Then al-Dawwani adds a third advantage: the definition is safe from the objection that the common definition ('perceiving that the proposition is true or not true') includes imagination (takhyil), doubt (shakk), and conjecture (wahm). These are perceptions of occurrence or non-occurrence but lack the element of acquiescence. Abu al-Fath clarifies these terms: imagination is conception without hesitation or supposition, doubt is conception with hesitation, conjecture is supposition of one side with leaning. A possible defense of the common definition is that the phrase 'perceiving that the proposition is true or not true' implies acquiescence by its wording, unlike 'occurrence or non-occurrence'. However, Mir Zahid weakens this defense: the phrase can still be understood as mere perception of occurrence, not necessarily with acquiescence. Thus, the author's definition using 'iqtinan' is more precise.

Key Terms
تصديق
إذعان
تخييل
شك
وهم

Key Takeaway
The definition of tasdiq must include iqtinan to exclude mere perception of occurrence without submission, ensuring precise logical and legal reasoning.

How Hukm's Nature Determines Tasdiq's Composition
Examines whether hukm is perception or action, affecting the count of tasawwurat in tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the number of tasawwurat in tasdiq given whether hukm is classified as perception or act.

Core Idea
Tasdiq composition depends on whether hukm is a perception or an act.

This passage examines a key debate in Islamic logic: whether hukm (judgment) is a perception (idrak) or an act (fi'l). The answer directly affects how many tasawwurat (conceptions) compose tasdiq (assent). Understanding this helps you see how logical structure underpins knowledge claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possibilities for hukm
The passage states that hukm could be either a perception (idrak) or an act (fi'l).
These are the only two options considered.
2
If hukm is an act, analyze composition
If hukm is an act, it is distinct from perception (since perception is passivity). Then tasdiq is composed of three tasawwurat plus the hukm. This totals four components, but hukm is not a tasawwur.
3
If hukm is a perception, analyze composition
If hukm is a perception, it would itself be a tasawwur, making tasdiq consist of four tasawwurat. But the commentator al-Dusuqi points out that each tasawwur would then need another tasawwur to be conceived, leading to infinite regress (tasalsul).
This regress is a key argument against hukm as perception.
4
Understand the resolution
The passage implies that hukm as an act avoids the regress because the act of judging does not itself require a separate conception. Thus, the view that hukm is an act is viable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كانَ فِعْلاً - والفعلُ مُغاير للإدراك ؛ إذ الإدراك انفعال والفعل يغايره ـ ؛ فحينئذ يكون التصديق مركباً مِنَ التَّصوراتِ الثَّلاثةِ والحُكْم . الدسوقي لأنَّ تصرُّرَ تلكَ التَّصوراتِ يحتاج أيضاً إلى تصور ، وتصوره يحتاج إلى تصور آخر وهكذا، فلا يحصلُ التَّصديقُ ، وحينئذ ؛ فتكونُ التَّصوّرات الأربعة حاصلة غير مُتصوَّرة . نعم إن حكم على تصوُّرٍ من تلكَ التَّصوراتِ بأنَّه موجودٌ مثلاً ؛ توقَّفَ التَّصديقُ بأنَّه موجودٌ على تصوُّرِ ذلك التَّصور، ولا يحتاج ذلك النَّصور إلى أن يتصوَّرَ لِمَا يلزمُ عليهِ مِنَ التّسلسل . (قَوْلُهُ : وَإِنْ كَانَ فِعْلَا ) أي : وإنْ كانَ الحكمُ فِعْلاً ، وجواب (إنْ)؛ قوله : (فحينئذ) وَمَا بينَهما جملة حاليَّةٌ أو اعتراضيَّة، وهذا مُقابل لِقَولِهِ سابقاً (فإنْ كانَ إدراكاً . . . إلخ) . فإنْ قُلْتَ على القول بأنَّهُ فِعْل ؛ كيفَ يتّصفُ بالبداهة والكسب معَ أنَّ الأفعال لا تتصف بهما ؟ . قُلْتُ : أصحابُ هذا القول يمنعونَ كونَ جميع الأفعال لا توصف بهما، ويقولونَ: إِنَّ بعض الأفعالِ يتّصفُ بهما، فإنْ توقَّفَ الفعلُ النَّفسي على أمورٍ مَعلومةٍ وترتب عليها ؛ فهوَ كَسبيٌّ ، وإلا ؛ فبديهي (قَوْلُهُ : إِذِ الْإِدْرَاكُ انْفِعَالُ هذا إِنَّما يصح إذا فُسِّرَ الإدراك بانتقاش الصُّورةِ الحاصلة منَ الشَّيء في العقل كما سبق. وأمَّا إذا فُسِّرَ بالصُّورة الحاصلة في العقل؛ كانَ كيفاً لا انفعالاً، وهذا هو التحقيق، وحينئذ ؛ فلا يكون الإدراك انفعالاً، كما لا يكونُ فِعْلاً.
And if it [judgment] is an act – and the act is different from perception, since perception is a passivity and the act differs from it – then at that time tasdiq is composed of the three tasawwurat and the judgment. Al-Dusuqi: Because the conceptualization of those tasawwurat also requires a tasawwur, and its conceptualization requires another tasawwur, and so on, so tasdiq would not be obtained; at that time the four tasawwurat would be obtained but not conceptualized. Yes, if one judges one of those tasawwurat as existent, for example, then the tasdiq that it is existent depends on the conceptualization of that tasawwur, and that tasawwur does not need to be conceptualized due to the regress that would follow. (His statement: 'and if it is an act') means: if the judgment is an act, and the answer to 'if' is his statement 'then at that time', and what is between them is a circumstantial or parenthetical clause. This is the counterpart to his earlier statement 'if it is a perception...etc.' If you say: on the view that it is an act, how is it described as intuitive (badihi) and acquired (kasbi) while actions are not described by these? I say: The proponents of this view deny that all actions are not described thereby, and they say: some actions are described thereby. If the mental act depends on known matters and results from them, it is acquired; otherwise it is intuitive. (His statement: 'since perception is passivity') This is only correct if perception is interpreted as the impression of the form obtained from the thing in the intellect, as previously. But if it is interpreted as the form present in the intellect, it is a quality, not a passivity. And this is the verified view, and at that time perception is not passivity, just as it is not an act.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage defines the composition of tasdiq (assent) by examining the nature of hukm (judgment). The author presents two possibilities: judgment is either a perception (idrak) or an act (fi'l). If judgment is an act, it is distinct from perception (since perception is passivity), and then tasdiq is composed of three tasawwurat (conceptions) plus the judgment. The commentator al-Dusuqi elaborates that if judgment were a perception, there would be four tasawwurat, but that leads to an infinite regress because each tasawwur would need another tasawwur. He also addresses an objection: how can an action be intuitive or acquired if actions are not described as such? The response is that some actions, specifically mental acts, can be described that way. Finally, the nature of idrak is clarified: when interpreted as the form in the intellect, it is a quality, not a passivity, and thus not an act either. This reinforces that judgment, if an act, is not a perception.

Key Terms
تصديق
حكم
إدراك
فعل

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when hukm is considered an act, how many tasawwurat compose tasdiq?
A) Four tasawwurat.
B) Three tasawwurat and the hukm.
C) Two tasawwurat and the hukm.
D) Only one tasawwur.

Key Takeaway
The composition of tasdiq hinges on whether hukm is an act (three tasawwurat + hukm) or a perception (four tasawwurat, rejected).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the legal proposition: 'Every intoxicant is prohibited.' Identify the number of tasawwurat and the hukm in this tasdiq, assuming hukm is an act. Explain each component.

Can a Mental Act Be Intuitive or Acquired?
Examines whether hukm is perception or action, affecting the count of tasawwurat in tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how hukm as a mental act can be described as badihi (intuitive) or kasbi (acquired).

Core Idea
Mental acts can be intuitive or acquired, contrary to the claim that all acts lack such description.

An objection is raised: if hukm is an act, how can it be intuitive or acquired, since actions are not described by those attributes? The passage provides the proponents' response, clarifying that some mental acts are indeed characterized as intuitive if they don't depend on prior knowledge, or acquired if they do. This lesson unpacks that dialectical exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The imaginary questioner asks: if hukm is an act (fi'l), how can it be described as badihi or kasbi? The assumption is that actions are not described as intuitive or acquired.
2
Locate the proponents' response
The author responds that proponents of the act-view deny that all actions are undescribable by these terms. They assert that some actions are indeed described as such.
3
Understand the criterion for intuitive vs. acquired
The response specifies: if the mental act depends on known matters and results from them, it is acquired (kasbi); otherwise, it is intuitive (badihi).
This criterion applies to mental acts, not physical ones.
4
Apply to hukm
Thus, hukm as a mental act can be intuitive if it is self-evident (e.g., 'The whole is greater than the part') or acquired if it is inferred from premises (e.g., a conclusion from a syllogism).

Redefining Idrak: Perception as Form vs. Passivity
Examines whether hukm is perception or action, affecting the count of tasawwurat in tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between two interpretations of idrak (perception) and explain their impact on the nature of hukm.

Core Idea
Whether idrak is passive impression or the mental form itself determines if hukm can be a perception.

The passage concludes by clarifying that idrak can be defined in two ways: as the passive impression (infi'al) or as the mental form (kayf). This distinction is crucial because if idrak is the form itself, it is a quality, not an act or passivity. Then hukm cannot be a passive perception, reinforcing the view that it is an act.

Guided Path
1
Recall the standard definition of idrak
Earlier in the tradition, idrak is defined as the passive impression (intiqa' al-sura) of a form from the object in the intellect. This is passivity (infi'al).
2
Identify the alternative interpretation
The passage provides a new interpretation: idrak can be understood as the form itself present in the intellect (al-sura al-hasila fi al-'aql). In this sense, it is a quality (kayf), not a passivity.
This is called 'al-tahqiq' (the verified view).
3
Understand implications for hukm
If idrak is a quality, then perception is neither an act nor a passivity. Therefore, if hukm were a perception, it would be a quality, not an act. But the passage seems to maintain that hukm is an act, not a quality.
This leaves open the possibility that hukm is a distinct act, not reducible to perception.
4
Summarize the logical move
By redefining idrak, the author prevents hukm from being classified as a passive perception (which would cause regress) and supports the act-view without giving up the concept of perception entirely.

5 min
The Division of Conception and Assent into Necessary and Acquired
Commentator explains the division of conception and assent into necessary and acquired.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the division of tasawwur and tasdiq into necessary (daruri) and acquired (kasbi), and explain the meaning of 'darura' as self-evidence in this context.

Core Idea
Conception and assent are each divided into necessary and acquired knowledge.

The author states that conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq) are divided by necessity (darura). The commentator explains that 'darura' here means self-evidence (badahah), not certainty. This division is fundamental in Islamic logic, as it distinguishes immediate knowledge from knowledge obtained through reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the divided items
The text says 'they are divided' (yanqasimani), referring to tasawwur and tasdiq. These are the two main categories of knowledge in logic.
Tasawwur is mental representation without judgment; tasdiq is judgment.
2
Understand the division basis
The division is 'by necessity' (bi-d-darura), meaning each is either necessary (self-evident) or acquired (obtained through reasoning).
The preposition 'ba' indicates accompaniment.
3
Clarify the meaning of darura
The commentator notes darura could mean self-evidence (badahah) or certainty (tat'ah); the apparent meaning is self-evidence.
Self-evident knowledge requires no proof, like the impossibility of a thing being both existent and non-existent.
4
Recognize the logical relationship
The necessary and acquired are not contradictory opposites but like contrariety or privation and possession, as later clarified.
This avoids the error of thinking every subject must be either necessary or acquired.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتنِ (وَيَنْقَسِمَانِ) ؛
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : وَيَنْقَسِمَانِ ... إلخ) شروعٌ فيما هو تمهيد للحاجة، والحاجة عصمة الذهن عن الخطأ في الفكر المشارِ لهُ بقولِهِ : فاحتيج إلى قانون . . . إلخ.
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : وَيَنْقَسِمَانِ) تقدَّمَ وجه تأخير هذا التَّقسيم عن الَّذي قبله، ثمَّ إِنَّ هَهُنا نُسختان (۱) ؛ الأُولى: ينقسمان من باب الانفعال، وذكر إلى الجارة في قوله : الضَّرورة، وعليها كتب الشارح، وهي ظاهرة لا تحتاج إلا لأن يرادَ مِنَ الضَّرورةِ والاكتسابِ الضَّروري والمكتسب ؛ لأنَّهما القِسمانِ مِنَ التَّصورِ والتَّصديق، وقد أشارَ لِذلكَ الشَّارحُ بقوله : وإِنَّما كانَ تقسيم ... إلخ، وأيضاً المقسم يحمل على القسم في تقسيم الكلي إلى جزئيَّاتِهِ كما هنا، وبدونِ التَّأويل لا يستقيمُ الحَمْلُ، وقد يصح إبقاؤها بلا تأويل ؛ بناءً على وضع قيدِ القسم مكانَ القسم؛ كَتَقسيم الحيوانِ إلى النَّاطِقِ والصَّاهِل، فالقِسمُ هَهُنا علمٌ ذو ضرورةٍ، وعلم ذو كسب، وهو معنى ضروري وكسبي، الثانية: ما كتب عليها الجلالُ الدَّوَانيُّ والعصامُ، وهي: ويقتسمان من باب الافتعال وحذف إلى الجارة، وهي محتملة لأن يقرأ بالبناء للفاعل، والضَّرورة والاكتساب بمعنى الضَّروريّ والمكتسب . . . إلخ، ما قلنا، ويرد على هذا الاحتمال اقتضاؤُهُ تقسيم الضَّروريّ والنَّظري إلى تَصوُّرٍ وتَصديقٍ؛ لأنَّ المعنى حينئذٍ يقسمُ التّصور والتصديق الضَّروري والمكتسب؛ أي: يحصل كلّ منهما قسماً من الضَّروريّ والمكتسب؛ فيكونُ كُلَّ مِنَ الضَّروريّ والمكتَسَبِ مُقسَّماً، والمفروضُ خِلافُهُ ؛ وهو أنَّ المقسَّم هو التَّصوُّرُ والتَّصديقُ ؛ لا أنَّهما قِسمَانِ، وأن يقرأ بالبناء للمفعول، والضَّرورة والاكتساب منصوبان على نزع الخافِضِ، وفيهما مِنَ التَّأويلِ مَا قُلنَا، وما أورد عليه بأنَّ النَّصبَ على نزع الخافض مقصورٌ على السَّماعِ ؛ يُجاب عنه بأنَّهُ كَثُرَ في كلامِهِم حَتَّى عُدَّ مِنَ المسامحات، وهَذان الاحتمالانِ مبنيَّانِ على ما ذكرَهُ في الأساس مِن أَنَّ قسمه واقتسمه بمعنى،
(1) (قولُهُ: نسختان) كذا بالنسخة التي بأيدينا ، والصَّوابُ نُسختَيْنِ بِالنَّصبِ؛ لأنَّه اسم «إِنَّ» مؤخراً عن خبرها الظَّرف . ا.هـ. الشَّرنوبي.

أي : التَصوُّرُ والتَّصديقُ (بِالضَّرُورَةِ)؛
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : بِالضَّرُورَةِ . . . إِلَخ الباءُ لِلملابسة؛ أي: انقساماً ملتبساً بالضرورة، ثمَّ يحتمل أن يكون المراد بالضَّرورة البداهة، وأن يكون المراد بها التَّطْعَ، والظَّاهِرُ الأول، وحينئذ؛ فقولُ الشَّارح : وإِنَّما كان تقسيم ... إلخ، من باب التنبيه لا من
العطار
وما في التسهيل من أنَّ افتعل يكون بمعنى فعل، وفسَّرَ الدَّوَّاني الاقتسام بالأخذ؛ حيث قال : أي يأخذُ كلٌّ مِنَ التَّصورِ والتَّصديقِ قِسماً من الضرورة والاكتساب؛ أي : الضَّروريّ والمكتسب .ا.هـ. فالضَّرورة والاكتساب مفعولان، قال العصام : وهوَ نِعْمَ التَّوجيه لو ساعده اللُّغة، ولم نجد في كتبِ اللُّغةِ أنَّ الافتعال يجي للاتِّخاذ، وقد يوجه بأنَّ المرادَ : يَقتسمان بينهما، ويلزمه أنْ يأخذ كلَّ مِنْهُمَا قِسماً ؛ انتهى. وأُجيب بثبوتِ مجيء الافتعال بمعنى الأخذ؛ نحو: ارتفق زيداً: أي: اتَّخَذَهُ رفيقاً، وهناك احتمال ثالث مبني على مجيء اقتسم بمعنى تقاسم؛ فقد ذكر التّسهيل مِن معاني افتعل تفاعل؛ فيقرأ يقتسمان بالبناء للفاعل، والضَّرورة والنَّظرُ على ظَاهرِهما مِن غير تأويل؛ مفعولان ليقتسمان، والمعنى حينئذ يأخذُ التَّصوُّرُ قِسماً من الضَّرورةِ؛ فيتحقَّقُ قسم ضروري، وقسماً مِنَ الاكتساب؛ فيتحقَّقُ تَصوُّرٌ مُكتسب، ويُقالُ مثله في التصديق ؛ فهو على حد قول الشاعر :
في كما صنع إنَّا اقتَسَمْنَا خُطَّتَيْنَا بِينَنَا فَحَمَلْتُ بَرَّةً واحتمَلتَ فَجار
(قَوْلُهُ : أَيْ : التَّصَوُّرُ والتَّصْدِيقُ) تقديمُ التَّصوُّرِ هنا على التصديق دون العكس المصنِّفُ؛ لأنَّ المنظور إليهِ هَهُنا ماصدقهما وأفرادهما، فإنَّهُ الَّذي يوصفُ بالضَّرورةِ والكَسْبِ ، وأمَّا مفهومُهُما ؛ فهو نظري كما سيأتي، قالَ شَارِحُ سُلَّم العلوم: ليس بين الضَّروري والكسبي تقابلُ الإيجابِ والسَّلبِ؛ لأنَّ المتقابلين بالإيجاب والسَّلبِ لا يخلو موضوع ما عنهُما ، وإلا ؛ لزم ارتفاعُ النَّقيضين، والموجوداتُ الغيبيَّةُ كُلُّها خالية عنهما، ولا التّضايفُ، وهو ظاهر، بل إنَّما يتصوَّرُ التّضادُّ أو العدمُ والمَلَكةُ، ولا بُدَّ في التَّضادّ من إمكان تعاقبهما على موضوع
Introduction of the author: (And they are divided) 
Dasuqi: (His statement: And they are divided ... etc.) is a start of what is a prelude for the need, and the need is the preservation of the mind from error in thinking referred to by his statement: 'So there is need for a rule ... etc.' 
Attar: (His statement: And they are divided) The reason for delaying this division after the one before it has preceded. Then there are two copies: The first: 'yanqasimani' from the passive form, and he mentioned the preposition 'ila' in his statement 'al-darura', and upon it the commentator wrote, and it is apparent, needing only that by 'darura' and 'iktisab' is meant the necessary and the acquired; because they are the two divisions of conception and assent. The commentator indicated this by his statement: 'And indeed the division was ... etc.' Also, the thing divided is carried upon the division in dividing the universal into its particulars as here, and without interpretation the carrying is not sound. It may be correct to leave it without interpretation based on placing the term 'division' in place of 'the divided'; like dividing animal into rational and neighing, so the division here is knowledge with necessity and knowledge with acquisition, meaning necessary and acquired. The second: What al-Jalal al-Dawani and al-Isam wrote upon, which is: 'yaqtasimani' from the ifti'al form, and the preposition 'ila' is omitted, and it is possible to read it as active voice, and 'al-darura' and 'al-iktisab' meaning the necessary and the acquired ... etc., as we said. An objection to this possibility is that it necessitates dividing the necessary and theoretical into conception and assent; because the meaning then is that conception and assent divide the necessary and acquired; i.e., each of them obtains a portion of the necessary and acquired; thus each of the necessary and acquired becomes divided, and the assumed is the opposite; namely that the divided is conception and assent, not that they are two divisions. And that it be read as passive, and 'al-darura' and 'al-iktisab' are in the accusative by removal of the preposition, and in them is the interpretation we mentioned. What is objected to this—that the accusative by removal of the preposition is restricted to hearing—is answered by that it has become frequent in their speech until it is considered among allowances. These two possibilities are based on what was mentioned in al-Asas that 'qasamahu' and 'iqtasamahu' are synonymous. 
(1) (His statement: two copies) Thus in the copy in our possession, but the correct is 'nuskhatayni' in the accusative because it is the noun of 'inna' delayed after its predicate, the adverb. End. al-Sharnubi. 
Meaning: conception and assent (by necessity); 
Dasuqi: (His statement: by necessity ... etc.) The preposition 'ba' is for accompaniment; i.e., a division accompanied by necessity. Then it is possible that by 'darura' is meant self-evidence, and that by it is meant certainty, and the apparent is the first. Then his statement: 'And indeed the division was ... etc.' is of the type of alerting, not of ... 
Attar: And what is in al-Tashil that 'ifta'ala' can have the meaning of 'fa'ala', and al-Dawani interpreted 'iqtisam' as taking; where he said: i.e., each of conception and assent takes a portion of necessity and acquisition; i.e., the necessary and the acquired. End. So 'al-darura' and 'al-iktisab' are objects. al-Isam said: It is an excellent interpretation if language supported it, and we do not find in books of language that 'ifti'al' comes for taking. It may be interpreted that the meaning is they divide between themselves, and it follows that each of them takes a portion; end. It was answered by the proof that 'ifti'al' comes with the meaning of taking; like 'irtadaqa Zaydan' i.e., made him a companion. There is a third possibility based on 'iqtasama' coming with the meaning of 'taqasama'; for al-Tashil mentions among the meanings of 'ifta'ala' is 'tafa'ala'; so it is read 'yaqtasimani' as active voice, and 'al-darura' and 'al-nazar' are on their apparent meaning without interpretation, as objects of 'yaqtasimani', and the meaning then is that conception takes a portion of necessity, so a necessary division is realized, and a portion of acquisition, so an acquired conception is realized, and the same is said concerning assent; it is like the poet's saying: 
'Indeed we divided our two lines between us, so I carried the good and you carried the wicked.' 
(His statement: i.e., conception and assent) Here he gives precedence to conception over assent, unlike the author's reverse, because what is looked at here is their referents and individuals, for they are described by necessity and acquisition. As for their concept, it is theoretical as will come. The commentator on Sullam al-Ulum said: There is not between the necessary and the acquired an opposition of affirmation and negation; because the two opposites by affirmation and negation do not have a subject devoid of both, otherwise the removal of the two contradictories would be necessary, and all unseen existences are devoid of them. Nor is it correlativity, which is apparent. Rather only contrariety or privation and possession can be imagined, and in contrariety there must be the possibility of them alternating upon a subject.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn's statement 'And they are divided' (wa yanqasimani), referring to tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent). The commentator, using the works of Dasuqi and Attar, explains the division of these two into necessary (daruri) and acquired (kasbi). The passage begins by identifying the text as the author's introduction, and then discusses the textual variants in the wording. There are two manuscript readings: one with the passive verb 'yanqasimani' (from infi'al) including the preposition 'ila', and another with the active verb 'yaqtasimani' (from ifti'al) without the preposition. The commentator analyzes each reading, noting the need for interpretation. The first reading, 'yanqasimani bi-d-darura', is taken as 'they are divided by necessity', where 'darura' means the necessary. The second reading, 'yaqtasimani', means 'they take portions', and the commentator objects that this would imply dividing necessary and theoretical into conception and assent, which reverses the intended division. The discussion includes grammatical points, such as the accusative case by removal of a preposition, and references to linguistic works like al-Asas and al-Tashil. A third possibility is that 'yaqtasimani' has the meaning of mutual division, as in the poet's verse. The passage then explains the meaning of 'bi-d-darura', noting that the preposition 'ba' indicates accompaniment, and 'darura' could mean self-evidence or certainty, with the first being more apparent. Finally, the passage addresses the order of mentioning conception before assent, and quotes a commentator on Sullam al-Ulum to clarify that the relationship between necessary and acquired is not that of contradictory opposites, but rather of contrariety or privation and possession. Throughout, the commentator emphasizes the precise wording and its implications for understanding the epistemological division. The passage is a detailed grammatical and logical analysis, typical of a sharh that expands on a compact matn statement.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the apparent meaning of 'darura' in the phrase 'yanqasimani bi-d-darura'?
A) Certainty (اليقين)
B) Necessity (الوجوب)
C) Self-evidence (البداهة)
D) Continuity (الدوام)

Key Takeaway
Conception and assent are each divided into self-evident (daruri) and acquired (kasbi), with 'darura' meaning self-evidence in this context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether the following is daruri or kasbi: 'The world has a creator' (a proposition debated in Kalam). Explain your reasoning based on the definition of darura as self-evidence.
?
Given a statement from a fiqh text: 'The obligation of zakat is known by necessity,' determine if this usage matches the logical definition of darura as explained in this lesson.

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
7 min
Textual Variants in Manuscripts of Mantiq
Commentator analyzes two manuscript readings of the verb 'they are divided' and their logical consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the differences between the two manuscript readings of the division phrase ('yanqasimani' vs 'yaqtasimani') and evaluate their logical implications.

Core Idea
A single verb change can reverse the direction of division in logic.

The commentator identifies two manuscript readings for the verb 'they are divided': one passive (yanqasimani) and one active (yaqtasimani). Each reading subtly changes the meaning of how conception and assent relate to the categories of necessary and acquired. Understanding these variants is crucial for correctly interpreting the logical structure of the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two manuscript readings
First reading: 'yanqasimani' from the passive form (infi'al) with the preposition 'ila'. Second reading: 'yaqtasimani' from the active form (ifti'al) without the preposition.
These are found in different copies of the text.
2
Analyze the grammatical structure of each
In the first, 'yanqasimani ila al-darura' means they are divided into necessity, with 'darura' and 'iktisab' as the divisions. In the second, 'yaqtasimani' can be read as active or passive, leading to different interpretations.
The active reading implies conception and assent take portions of necessity and acquisition.
3
Evaluate the logical implications
The second reading, if taken as active, would make the necessary and acquired the divided items, not the divisions. This reverses the intended meaning, so interpretation is needed.
The commentator objects to this reversal.
4
Consider the proposed resolutions
One resolution is to read it as passive with accusative by removal of preposition. Another is to accept 'iqtasama' as synonymous with 'qasama', or as mutual division like 'taqasama'.
These rely on linguistic attestations from works like al-Asas and al-Tashil.
