Two Answers to an Objection and the Benefit on Partial vs. Universal Sciences
Presents two answers to an objection and a benefit on partial vs. universal sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the investigation of specific states can be justified as subsidiary to universal sciences, and identify the two answers given to the objection about subject matters as presented by Abu al-Fath and 'Abd al-Hakim.

Core Idea
Partial sciences study specific accidents under universal sciences, either by direct investigation or by incidental inclusion.

After defining accidental accidents, al-Dasuqi faces an objection: how can a science investigate accidents specific to its subject's types? Two answers are provided by Abu al-Fath, and a clarifying benefit from 'Abd al-Hakim shows the relationship between universal and partial sciences. This discussion illuminates the hierarchical structure of knowledge in the Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objection is that a universal science (like natural science) studies its subject (body) universally, but accidents specific to types of body (e.g., sphere) are partial. How can natural science investigate them?
This objection arises from the definition of a science's subject matter.
2
Extract the first answer
The first answer: investigation of specific states may occur 'in the manner of extrapolation/extension' (على سبيل التَّطقُلِ). This likely means by extension or as a perfection of the subject.
The Arabic word is ambiguous; it may mean 'by way of intrusion' or 'by way of completion'.
3
Extract the second answer
The second answer: investigation reduces to the common essential accidents that include the specific states incidentally. The specific states are studied not in themselves but as included in the common states.
This makes the partial science subordinate to the universal.
4
Analyse the benefit from 'Abd al-Hakim
'Abd al-Hakim clarifies that partial sciences are encompassed by universal sciences: e.g., sphere science (partial) under natural science (universal). The accidents of sphere are studied in sphere science, while natural science studies body as such.
Thus, the partial science is a branch of the universal science.
5
Evaluate the strength of these answers
Abu al-Fath says the two possibilities are not apparent, but the inclusion of publication (ضَمَّ النَّشرِ) is better. Later scholars may adopt one of the interpretations for the sake of justification.
This shows a pragmatic approach to doctrinal consistency.

Source Text

The Logician's Perspective on Words
Author explains the third reason for studying words and rebuts an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why logicians study words specifically as indicators of meanings and how this rebuts a potential objection about the order of studying indication.

Core Idea
Logicians study words not as grammar, but as universal indicators of meaning.

This lesson unpacks the third reason for studying words: that they are 'considered' (manẓūr fīhā) from a specific perspective. Al-Dasuqi clarifies that words are examined as indicators of meanings, not as singular or compound entities, accidents, or existents. This perspective solves an apparent problem: if indication is an attribute of words, shouldn't words be studied first? Because words are studied as indicators, the study of indication follows naturally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context: three reasons for studying words
The author lists three reasons; this passage introduces the third. Refer to the preceding lessons to see that the first two reasons are not detailed here.
2
Extract the specific perspective on words
Al-Dasuqi explicitly states what words are NOT studied for: they are not studied as singular or compound (grammatical units), not as accidents (physical properties), and not as existents in the mind or outside. The only remaining perspective is 'as indicators of meanings' (dala'il al-ma'ani).
3
Understand the rebutted objection
Someone might object that since indication (dalala) is an attribute of words, the discussion of words should precede that of indication. But because words are studied precisely as indicators, the attribute (indication) is inseparable; thus the order is appropriate.
4
Summarize the logician's definition of words in this context
In logic, words are considered (manẓūr fīhā) as bearers of indication, not for their own properties. This is a functional, universal perspective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في تعريف الدَّلالاتِ الثَّلاثِ وأحكامها

٣. وكَوْنِ الألفاظ منظوراً فيها

الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى الْأَلْفَاظِ) أي : فَاحتيج لمبحث الألفاظ. (قَوْلُهُ : وَكَوْنِ الْأَلْفَاظِ ) أي : المتوفّفُ عليها إفادة المعاني واستفادتُها ; منظوراً فيها من حيثُ إِنَّها دلائل المعاني; أي: لَا مِن حيثُ إِنَّهَا مُفردةٌ أَو مُركَّبة، وَلَا مِن حيثُ إِنَّها عَرَضُ، وَلَا مِن حيثُ إنَّها موجودةٌ خارجاً أو ذهناً، وبهذه الحيثية اندفع مَا يُقالُ : إِنَّ الدَّلالةَ وصفٌ لِلألفاظ، ومرتبةً الموصوفِ مُقدَّمةٌ على مرتبة الوصف فكانَ اللائقُ ذِكْرَ مباحث اللفظ قبل مباحثِ الدَّلالةِ .

العطار
هذه المباحث مناسبة للمباحِثِ المنطقيَّة، فإنّها أُمورٌ قَانونيَّةٌ مُتناولةٌ لِجَميعِ المفهومات، وربَّما يورد على الندرة أقوال مخصوصةٌ باللُّغةِ الَّتِي دُوِّنَ بِهَا هذا الفن لزيادة الاعتناء بها ا.هـ. فَعُلِمَ مِنْهُ اختلافُ يَحتَيْ أهل العربية والمناطقة عن أحوالِ الألفاظ، فإنَّ أهلَ العربيَّةِ يبحثون عنها على قاعدة لُغَةِ العرب، والمناطقة يبحثونَ عن أحوالِهَا الشَّاملة لجميع اللُّغَاتِ.
Chapter: On the definition of the three types of indication and their rulings.

3. And that words are considered.

Al-Dasuqi:
(His statement: 'words') i.e., so the discussion of words is needed. (His statement: 'and that words') i.e., upon which the communication and acquisition of meanings depend; considered from the perspective that they are indicators of meanings; i.e., not from the perspective that they are singular or compound, nor from the perspective that they are accidents, nor from the perspective that they exist externally or mentally. With this perspective, what is said is rebutted: that indication is an attribute of words, and the rank of the described precedes the rank of the attribute, so it would be appropriate to mention the discussions of words before the discussions of indication.

Al-Atar:
These discussions are appropriate to the logical discussions, for they are universal matters covering all concepts. And perhaps there are occasionally particular statements about the language in which this art is written, to increase attention to it. So it is known from this the difference between the concerns of the Arabic grammarians and the logicians regarding the states of words: the Arabic grammarians investigate them on the basis of the Arabic language, while the logicians investigate their universal states covering all languages.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter titled 'On the definition of the three types of indication and their rulings.' It then presents the third reason for studying words: 'And that words are considered.' Al-Dasuqi explains that words are needed, and they are considered not in themselves but as indicators of meanings. He notes that this perspective rebuts an objection: one might think that since indication (dalala) is an attribute of words, the study of words should precede the study of indication. However, because words are studied as indicators, the discussion of indication naturally follows. Al-Atar adds that the logical investigation of words is universal, covering all languages, unlike the Arabic grammarians who focus only on the Arabic language. Thus, this chapter sets the stage for examining the three types of indication: verbal, mental, and real (or customary, etc., though the specific types are not detailed here).

Key Terms
دلالة (dalāla): Indication; the attribute of words that points to meanings, studied in logic as a universal concept. [Note: No significant shift.]
ألفاظ (alfāẓ): Words, considered from the perspective of being indicators of meanings, not as physical or grammatical entities. [Note: No significant shift.]
منظور فيها (manẓūr fīhā): Considered; i.e., words are examined in logic with a specific perspective (as indicators). [Note: No significant shift.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Dasuqi, from what perspective are words studied in logic?
A) As physical sounds or written marks.
B) As indicators of meanings.
C) As singular or compound grammatical units.
D) As existing in the mind only.

Key Takeaway
Logic studies words universally as indicators of meanings, not as grammatical or physical entities.

Logic vs. Grammar: Universal vs. Particular
Al-Atar clarifies the difference between logical and grammatical investigations of words.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the logician's approach to words (universal) and the grammarian's approach (language-specific).

Core Idea
Logic studies words across all languages; grammar is confined to one language.

Al-Atar's commentary adds an important clarification: the logical investigation of words is universal, covering all concepts and languages, whereas the Arabic grammarians restrict themselves to the rules of Arabic. This distinction highlights the epistemological scope of logic and explains why logical principles about words apply to any language, including non-Arabic ones.

Guided Path
1
Locate al-Atar's statement about the difference
Al-Atar says: 'the difference between the concerns of the Arabic grammarians and the logicians regarding the states of words.'
2
Identify the scope of each discipline
Grammarians investigate on the basis of a specific language (Arabic); logicians investigate universal states covering all languages.
3
Understand why this distinction matters for logic
Logic provides tools that apply to any language, ensuring that the analysis of indication (dalala) is not culture-bound or limited to a particular linguistic system.
4
Give an example of a universal logical property of words
The concept of 'indication' (dalala) itself is universal; any language has words that indicate meanings by convention. This is a logical property, not a grammatical one.

Critique of 'تمام' in the Definition of مطابقية
Critique of the word 'تمام' in the definition of مطابقية

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the inclusion of the word 'تمام' in the definition of مطابقية and propose a correction based on al-Dasuqi's critique.

Core Idea
A definition must cover all instances; unnecessary conditions like 'تمام' may wrongly exclude simple concepts.

In this passage, al-Dasuqi critically examines the standard definition of correspondence indication. He argues that the condition 'تمام' (entirety) is problematic because it implies composition and would exclude simple meanings like 'point'. This lesson walks through his argument and the suggested fix.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under critique
The definition is 'دلالة اللفظ على تمام ما وضع له' (indication of the word upon the entirety of what it was placed for).
2
Understand the objection
Why does 'تمام' exclude simple meanings? Because it suggests parts, but simple concepts like 'point' have no parts.
3
Examine the attempted defense
Some said 'تمام' contrasts with 'نقص' (deficiency), not 'جزء' (part), so it doesn't imply composition.
4
Assess the final verdict
Al-Dasuqi argues that since 'تمام' is placed in contrast to 'جزء' in the definition of تضمنية, it does imply composition, so it's better to delete or replace with 'عين'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَلَى تَمَام مَا وُضِعَ اللَّفْظُ (لَهُ مُطابَقَةٌ)
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : (تمام) ذكرَهُ ؛ لرعاية مقابله، وهو قوله : على جزيه، وزيادة هذه اللفظة تخرج من التَّعريف دلالة اللفظ على المعنى البسيط ؛ كدلالة لفظ نقطة على نهاية الخطّ، فيكونُ التَّعريفُ غير جامع. وأجيبُ : بأنَّ (تمام) ؛ لا تشعرُ بالتَّركيبِ كَجميع؛ حتى يخرج دلالة اللفظ على المعنى البسيط؛ لأنَّه في مقابلةِ النَّقص، بخلافِ جميع ؛ فإنَّه في مقابلة البعض، وفيه : أنَّه ذكرها في مقابلة الجزء، وحينئذ ؛ فيكون دالا على التركيب، فَالأَوْلَى حَذْفُهُ أو إبداله بعين. (قَوْلُهُ : اللَّفْظِ) الأَوْلَى أنْ يأتي بأداةِ التَّفسير ؛ لأنَّهُ تفسير لنائب الفاعل، لَا أَنَّهُ نائب فاعل كما هو ظاهرُهُ، وفيه إشارة إلى أنَّ الصفة أو الصِّلةَ جَرَتْ على غيرِ مَنْ هِيَ له، فكانَ الواجب إبراز الضَّميرِ، إِلَّا أَنْ يُقالَ: إنَّهُ مشى على طريقةٍ مَن يقولُ : إِنَّهُ لا يجب الإبراز إذا كان الجاري على غير مَنْ هُوَ لهُ فعلاً، وإنَّما يجب في الوصف. (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى تَمَام مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ :أي: على المعنى الَّذِي وضع له بتمامه وعينه؛ بحيثُ لا يخرج شيءٌ مِمَّا اعتبره الواضع في مقابلته، وسواء كانَ اللَّفظ مشتركاً أو لا ؛ كان حقيقةً أو مجازاً ، فَدلالة المشتركِ على كلِّ مِنْ مَعانيهِ مُطابقةٌ، وَكَذا دلالةُ اللَّفْظ على معناه المجازي، كدلالة أسد على الرَّجُلِ الشُّجاع.
(قَوْلُهُ : مُطَابَقَةٌ) أي : تُسمَّى مُطابقة ؛ أي : دلالة مطابقة
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى تَمَامِ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ قيدُ التّمامِ غير ضروري في التَّعريفِ، بَلْ إِنَّمَا ذُكِرَ رعايةٌ لِمَا يقتضيهِ حُسْنُ التَّقابُلِ مَعَ الشَّقِّ الثَّاني، ولم يُعبّر بجميع لإشعاره بالتركيب،
(قَوْلُهُ : وسواء كان اللفظ ... إلخ) فيراد بالوضع ما يشمل التحقيقي وهو ما لا يحتاج إلى قرينة كالحقائق، والتأويلي وهو ما يحتاج لها كالمجازات والوضع الشخصي كبعض المفردات، والنوعي كالمشتقات والمركبات، وسواء كان الوضع عاماً لعام كوضع الكليات أو عاماً لخاص كالموصولات وأسماء الإشارة على التحقيق من أنها كليات وضعاً جزئيات استعمالاً، خلافاً للمصنف أو خاصَّاً لخاص كوضع الأعلام الشخصية، ويشترط في المشترك وجود القرينة حتى لا تكون دلالته مطابقية .
Upon the entirety of what the word was placed for (is called) correspondence. al-Dasuqi: 'His saying: "entirety" (tamam) he mentioned it for the sake of its opposite, i.e., his saying "upon its part" (juz'ihi). And the addition of this word excludes from the definition the indication of the word for the simple meaning (al-ma'na al-basit), like the indication of the word 'point' for the end of a line, so the definition would not be comprehensive. And it was answered: that "tamam" does not imply composition like "kull" (all) such that it would exclude the indication of the word for the simple meaning, because it is in contrast to "naqs" (deficiency), unlike "kull" which is in contrast to "ba'd" (some). But there is the point: He mentioned it in contrast to "juz'" (part), and therefore it does imply composition. So the best is to delete it or replace it with 'ayn (self). His saying: "the word" (al-lafz) - it would be better to bring the tool of interpretation (adatal-tafsir) because it is an interpretation of the agent noun (na'ib al-fa'il), not that it is the agent noun as it appears. And in it is an indication that the adjective or relative clause proceeded upon other than the one it is for, so it was necessary to bring out the pronoun, unless it is said that he followed the way of those who say that the pronoun does not have to be brought out when the proceeding is upon other than the one it is for in actuality, and it is only obligatory in the description. His saying: "upon the entirety of what it was placed for" i.e., upon the meaning for which it was placed in its entirety and its very self, such that nothing of what the inventor considered in its opposite exits. And whether the word is homonymous (mushtarak) or not, whether it is literal (haqiqa) or metaphorical (majaz). So the indication of a homonym for each of its meanings is correspondence, and likewise the indication of a word for its metaphorical meaning, like the indication of 'asad' (lion) for the brave man. His saying: "correspondence" (mutabaqa) i.e., it is called mutabaqa, i.e., a correspondence indication. al-'Attar: 'His saying: "upon the entirety of what it was placed for" - the condition of entirety (qayd al-tamam) is not necessary in the definition, rather it was only mentioned for the sake of good correspondence with the second division (i.e., containment), and he did not use 'kull' because it suggests composition. His saying: "and whether the word is homonymous... etc." - by wad' (convention) is meant what includes the investigative (tahqiqi) which needs no context (qarina) like literal expressions, and the interpretive (ta'wili) which needs it like metaphors, and the personal convention (wad' shakhsi) like some singulars, and the generic convention (wad' naw'i) like derived terms and compounds. And whether the convention is general for general like the placing of universals, or general for particular like relative pronouns and demonstrative pronouns according to the verification that they are universals in placement and particulars in usage, contrary to the author, or particular for particular like the placing of proper nouns. And it is required for the homonym that there be a context to prevent its indication from being correspondence.'
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the definition of 'correspondence indication' (dalala mutabaqiyya). The commentator al-Dasuqi begins by noting a problem in the definition: the inclusion of the word 'تمام' (entirety). The definition was presumably 'the indication of a word upon the entirety of what it was placed for'. The critic argues that this word 'تمام' is problematic because it would exclude simple meanings like 'point' (which has no parts), making the definition not comprehensive. The response is that 'تمام' does not imply composition like 'جميع' (all) does, because it contrasts with 'نقص' (deficiency) rather than 'بعض' (some). However, the commentator points out that since 'تمام' was mentioned in contrast to 'جزء' (part), it does imply composition after all. Therefore, the best course is to delete 'تمام' or replace it with 'عين' (self/essence). Then he discusses another point: the word 'اللفظ' (the word) in the definition should grammatically be interpreted as a 'تفسير' (exegesis) of the deputy subject (na'ib al-fa'il), not as the deputy subject itself, and he comments on the occasion of the pronoun. He then clarifies the meaning of 'على تمام ما وضع له': it means the meaning for which the word was coined in its entirety and essence, so that nothing considered by the inventor is excluded. This applies whether the word is homonymous, literal, or metaphorical. For example, the word 'أسد' (lion) indicates the brave man metaphorically, and that indication is correspondence because it indicates the entire transferred meaning. Then al-'Attar adds that the condition of 'تمام' is not necessary; it was only inserted for rhetorical symmetry with the second part (containment). He explains that the term 'وضع' (convention) used in the definition is comprehensive, covering various types: investigative (tahqiqi) for literal usage, interpretive (ta'wili) for metaphors, personal (shakhsi) for proper nouns, and generic (naw'i) for derived terms. He also discusses how conventions may be general or specific. Finally, he notes that for homonyms, a context (qarina) is needed to prevent the indication from being of the correspondence type (since without context, the word would not indicate any single meaning fully). This detailed critique shows the precision required in defining logical terms.

Key Terms
تمام
مطابقية
وضع
قرينة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because it implies composition and thus excludes simple meanings like 'point'.
C) Because it is not an Arabic word.
D) Because it contradicts the definition of تضمنية.

Key Takeaway
A definition must be comprehensive; extraneous conditions like 'تمام' that introduce implied composition should be avoided.

For example, consider the definition of 'قياس' (analogical reasoning) if it includes a condition that the 'علة' must be explicit—might such a condition exclude valid forms of قياس? Use the method of al-Dasuqi.

Types of Wad' and Condition for Homonyms in تعريف مطابقية
Explanation of types of wad' and condition for homonyms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify different types of wad' (convention) and explain why a homonym requires a قرينة for مطابقية indication.

Core Idea
Wad' encompasses literal, metaphorical, personal, and generic conventions; homonyms need context to achieve correspondence.

Al-'Attar expands the definition of مطابقية by clarifying the term 'وضع' (placement). He explains that it covers various types of convention and notes that for homonyms, a contextual clue is necessary to ensure the word indicates a single meaning completely. This lesson breaks down these nuances.

Guided Path
1
Understand the broad concept of wad'
Wad' includes investigative (tahqiqi), interpretive (ta'wili), personal (shakhsi), and generic (naw'i) conventions.
2
Identify examples for each type
Literal: 'أسد' for the animal; metaphorical: 'أسد' for a brave man; personal: proper noun 'زيد'; generic: derived terms like 'ضارب'.
3
Recognize the condition for homonyms
A homonym like 'عين' has multiple meanings; to indicate one specific meaning in correspondence, a qarina is required.
4
Connect to the definition of مطابقية
The definition does not require the word to be univocal; even homonyms can have correspondence if context specifies the intended meaning.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَلَى تَمَام مَا وُضِعَ اللَّفْظُ (لَهُ مُطابَقَةٌ)
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : (تمام) ذكرَهُ ؛ لرعاية مقابله، وهو قوله : على جزيه، وزيادة هذه اللفظة تخرج من التَّعريف دلالة اللفظ على المعنى البسيط ؛ كدلالة لفظ نقطة على نهاية الخطّ، فيكونُ التَّعريفُ غير جامع. وأجيبُ : بأنَّ (تمام) ؛ لا تشعرُ بالتَّركيبِ كَجميع؛ حتى يخرج دلالة اللفظ على المعنى البسيط؛ لأنَّه في مقابلةِ النَّقص، بخلافِ جميع ؛ فإنَّه في مقابلة البعض، وفيه : أنَّه ذكرها في مقابلة الجزء، وحينئذ ؛ فيكون دالا على التركيب، فَالأَوْلَى حَذْفُهُ أو إبداله بعين. (قَوْلُهُ : اللَّفْظِ) الأَوْلَى أنْ يأتي بأداةِ التَّفسير ؛ لأنَّهُ تفسير لنائب الفاعل، لَا أَنَّهُ نائب فاعل كما هو ظاهرُهُ، وفيه إشارة إلى أنَّ الصفة أو الصِّلةَ جَرَتْ على غيرِ مَنْ هِيَ له، فكانَ الواجب إبراز الضَّميرِ، إِلَّا أَنْ يُقالَ: إنَّهُ مشى على طريقةٍ مَن يقولُ : إِنَّهُ لا يجب الإبراز إذا كان الجاري على غير مَنْ هُوَ لهُ فعلاً، وإنَّما يجب في الوصف. (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى تَمَام مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ :أي: على المعنى الَّذِي وضع له بتمامه وعينه؛ بحيثُ لا يخرج شيءٌ مِمَّا اعتبره الواضع في مقابلته، وسواء كانَ اللَّفظ مشتركاً أو لا ؛ كان حقيقةً أو مجازاً ، فَدلالة المشتركِ على كلِّ مِنْ مَعانيهِ مُطابقةٌ، وَكَذا دلالةُ اللَّفْظ على معناه المجازي، كدلالة أسد على الرَّجُلِ الشُّجاع.
(قَوْلُهُ : مُطَابَقَةٌ) أي : تُسمَّى مُطابقة ؛ أي : دلالة مطابقة
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى تَمَامِ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ قيدُ التّمامِ غير ضروري في التَّعريفِ، بَلْ إِنَّمَا ذُكِرَ رعايةٌ لِمَا يقتضيهِ حُسْنُ التَّقابُلِ مَعَ الشَّقِّ الثَّاني، ولم يُعبّر بجميع لإشعاره بالتركيب،
(قَوْلُهُ : وسواء كان اللفظ ... إلخ) فيراد بالوضع ما يشمل التحقيقي وهو ما لا يحتاج إلى قرينة كالحقائق، والتأويلي وهو ما يحتاج لها كالمجازات والوضع الشخصي كبعض المفردات، والنوعي كالمشتقات والمركبات، وسواء كان الوضع عاماً لعام كوضع الكليات أو عاماً لخاص كالموصولات وأسماء الإشارة على التحقيق من أنها كليات وضعاً جزئيات استعمالاً، خلافاً للمصنف أو خاصَّاً لخاص كوضع الأعلام الشخصية، ويشترط في المشترك وجود القرينة حتى لا تكون دلالته مطابقية .
Upon the entirety of what the word was placed for (is called) correspondence. al-Dasuqi: 'His saying: "entirety" (tamam) he mentioned it for the sake of its opposite, i.e., his saying "upon its part" (juz'ihi). And the addition of this word excludes from the definition the indication of the word for the simple meaning (al-ma'na al-basit), like the indication of the word 'point' for the end of a line, so the definition would not be comprehensive. And it was answered: that "tamam" does not imply composition like "kull" (all) such that it would exclude the indication of the word for the simple meaning, because it is in contrast to "naqs" (deficiency), unlike "kull" which is in contrast to "ba'd" (some). But there is the point: He mentioned it in contrast to "juz'" (part), and therefore it does imply composition. So the best is to delete it or replace it with 'ayn (self). His saying: "the word" (al-lafz) - it would be better to bring the tool of interpretation (adatal-tafsir) because it is an interpretation of the agent noun (na'ib al-fa'il), not that it is the agent noun as it appears. And in it is an indication that the adjective or relative clause proceeded upon other than the one it is for, so it was necessary to bring out the pronoun, unless it is said that he followed the way of those who say that the pronoun does not have to be brought out when the proceeding is upon other than the one it is for in actuality, and it is only obligatory in the description. His saying: "upon the entirety of what it was placed for" i.e., upon the meaning for which it was placed in its entirety and its very self, such that nothing of what the inventor considered in its opposite exits. And whether the word is homonymous (mushtarak) or not, whether it is literal (haqiqa) or metaphorical (majaz). So the indication of a homonym for each of its meanings is correspondence, and likewise the indication of a word for its metaphorical meaning, like the indication of 'asad' (lion) for the brave man. His saying: "correspondence" (mutabaqa) i.e., it is called mutabaqa, i.e., a correspondence indication. al-'Attar: 'His saying: "upon the entirety of what it was placed for" - the condition of entirety (qayd al-tamam) is not necessary in the definition, rather it was only mentioned for the sake of good correspondence with the second division (i.e., containment), and he did not use 'kull' because it suggests composition. His saying: "and whether the word is homonymous... etc." - by wad' (convention) is meant what includes the investigative (tahqiqi) which needs no context (qarina) like literal expressions, and the interpretive (ta'wili) which needs it like metaphors, and the personal convention (wad' shakhsi) like some singulars, and the generic convention (wad' naw'i) like derived terms and compounds. And whether the convention is general for general like the placing of universals, or general for particular like relative pronouns and demonstrative pronouns according to the verification that they are universals in placement and particulars in usage, contrary to the author, or particular for particular like the placing of proper nouns. And it is required for the homonym that there be a context to prevent its indication from being correspondence.'
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the definition of 'correspondence indication' (dalala mutabaqiyya). The commentator al-Dasuqi begins by noting a problem in the definition: the inclusion of the word 'تمام' (entirety). The definition was presumably 'the indication of a word upon the entirety of what it was placed for'. The critic argues that this word 'تمام' is problematic because it would exclude simple meanings like 'point' (which has no parts), making the definition not comprehensive. The response is that 'تمام' does not imply composition like 'جميع' (all) does, because it contrasts with 'نقص' (deficiency) rather than 'بعض' (some). However, the commentator points out that since 'تمام' was mentioned in contrast to 'جزء' (part), it does imply composition after all. Therefore, the best course is to delete 'تمام' or replace it with 'عين' (self/essence). Then he discusses another point: the word 'اللفظ' (the word) in the definition should grammatically be interpreted as a 'تفسير' (exegesis) of the deputy subject (na'ib al-fa'il), not as the deputy subject itself, and he comments on the occasion of the pronoun. He then clarifies the meaning of 'على تمام ما وضع له': it means the meaning for which the word was coined in its entirety and essence, so that nothing considered by the inventor is excluded. This applies whether the word is homonymous, literal, or metaphorical. For example, the word 'أسد' (lion) indicates the brave man metaphorically, and that indication is correspondence because it indicates the entire transferred meaning. Then al-'Attar adds that the condition of 'تمام' is not necessary; it was only inserted for rhetorical symmetry with the second part (containment). He explains that the term 'وضع' (convention) used in the definition is comprehensive, covering various types: investigative (tahqiqi) for literal usage, interpretive (ta'wili) for metaphors, personal (shakhsi) for proper nouns, and generic (naw'i) for derived terms. He also discusses how conventions may be general or specific. Finally, he notes that for homonyms, a context (qarina) is needed to prevent the indication from being of the correspondence type (since without context, the word would not indicate any single meaning fully). This detailed critique shows the precision required in defining logical terms.

Key Terms
وضع
تحقيقي
تأويلي
شخصي
نوعي
قرينة
مشترك

Key Takeaway

The Critique of 'تمام' in Defining المطابقة
Al-Dasuqi critiques the inclusion of 'تمام' and al-Attar responds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why the word 'تمام' was considered problematic in the definition of mutābaqa and evaluate the arguments of al-Dasuqi and al-Attar.

Core Idea
The word 'تمام' in a definition can inadvertently imply composition, excluding simple concepts.

In this lesson, we examine a critical refinement in the definition of mutābaqa (correspondence indication). Al-Dasuqi raises an objection: the word 'تمام' (completeness) suggests composition, which would incorrectly exclude simple concepts like 'point' from the definition. Al-Attar responds, defending the inclusion of 'تمام' for symmetry. This exchange illustrates how careful wording is essential in logical definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under discussion
Find the definition of 'مطابقة' in the text: 'دلالة اللفظ على تمام ما وضع له'. Note the presence of 'تمام'.
The definition is about the indication of a word for the complete meaning it is placed for.
2
Understand al-Dasuqi's objection
Al-Dasuqi argues that 'تمام' implies composition because it contrasts with 'جزء' (part). This would exclude simple meanings like that of 'point' (نقطة), which indicates the end of a line without parts.
The definition would become non-comprehensive if it excludes simple concepts.
3
Examine the defense and counter-defense
Al-Dasuqi initially defends the definition by saying 'تمام' does not imply composition like 'جميع' (all), as it is opposite to 'نقص' (deficiency). But he then rejects this because 'تمام' is mentioned in contrast to 'جزء', so it does imply composition.
He ends up recommending deletion of 'تمام' or replacement with 'عين'.
4
Consider al-Attar's response
Al-Attar argues that 'تمام' is not necessary but is included for good contrast with the second branch (تضمن or التزام). It does not imply composition like 'جميع' would, so it is acceptable.
Al-Attar's view is that the word is kept for symmetry, not as a logical condition.
5
Reflect on the broader implications
This critique shows how a single word in a definition can affect its scope. In Usul al-Fiqh, similar care is needed when defining terms like 'علة' to avoid unintended implications.
The footnote clarifies that 'وضع' includes various types, affecting which indications count as مطابقة.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَلَى تَمَام مَا وُضِعَ اللَّفْظُ (لَهُ مُطابَقَةٌ) الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : (تمام) ذكرَهُ ؛ لرعاية مقابله، وهو قوله : على جزيه، وزيادة هذه اللفظة تخرج من التَّعريف دلالة اللفظ على المعنى البسيط ؛ كدلالة لفظ نقطة على نهاية الخطّ، فيكونُ التَّعريفُ غير جامع. وأجيبُ : بأنَّ (تمام) ؛ لا تشعرُ بالتَّركيبِ كَجميع؛ حتى يخرج دلالة اللفظ على المعنى البسيط؛ لأنَّه في مقابلةِ النَّقص، بخلافِ جميع ؛ فإنَّه في مقابلة البعض، وفيه : أنَّه ذكرها في مقابلة الجزء، وحينئذ ؛ فيكون دالا على التركيب، فَالأَوْلَى حَذْفُهُ حذفه أو إبداله بعين. (قَوْلُهُ : اللَّفْظِ) الأَوْلَى أنْ يأتي بأداةِ التَّفسير ؛ لأنَّهُ تفسير لنائب الفاعل، لَا أَنَّهُ نائب فاعل كما هو ظاهرُهُ، وفيه إشارة إلى أنَّ الصفة أو الصِّلةَ جَرَتْ على غيرِ مَنْ هِيَ له، فكانَ الواجب إبراز الضَّميرِ، إِلَّا أَنْ يُقالَ: إنَّهُ مشى على طريقةٍ مَن يقولُ : إِنَّهُ لا ليتي يجب الإبراز إذا كان الجاري على غير مَنْ هُوَ لهُ فعلاً، وإنَّما يجب في الوصف. (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى تَمَام مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ :أي: على المعنى الَّذِي وضع له بتمامه وعينه؛ بحيثُ لا يخرج شيءٌ مِمَّا اعتبره الواضع في مقابلته، وسواء كانَ اللَّفظ (۱) مشتركاً أو لا ؛ كان حقيقةً أو مجازاً ، فَدلالة المشتركِ على كلِّ مِنْ مَعانيهِ مُطابقةٌ، وَكَذا دلالةُ اللَّفْظ على معناه المجازي، كدلالة أسد على الرَّجُلِ الشُّجاع. (قَوْلُهُ : مُطَابَقَةٌ) أي : تُسمَّى مُطابقة ; أي : دلالة مطابقة العطار (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى تَمَامِ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ قيدُ التّمامِ غير ضروري في التَّعريفِ، بَلْ إِنَّمَا ذُكِرَ رعايةٌ لِمَا يقتضيهِ حُسْنُ التَّقابُلِ مَعَ الشَّقِّ الثَّاني، ولم يُعبّر بجميع لإشعاره بالتركيب، (۱) (قَوْلُهُ : وسواء كان اللفظ ... إلخ) فيراد بالوضع ما يشمل التحقيقي وهو ما لا يحتاج إلى قرينة كالحقائق، والتأويلي وهو ما يحتاج لها كالمجازات والوضع الشخصي كبعض المفردات، والنوعي كالمشتقات والمركبات، وسواء كان الوضع عاماً لعام كوضع الكليات أو عاماً لخاص كالموصولات وأسماء الإشارة على التحقيق من أنها كليات وضعاً جزئيات استعمالاً، خلافاً للمصنف أو خاصَّاً لخاص كوضع الأعلام الشخصية، ويشترط في المشترك وجود القرينة حتى لا تكون دلالته مطابقية .
Upon the completeness of what the word is placed for (correspondence). Al-Dasuqi: His statement: 'completeness' he mentioned it; for the sake of observing its counterpart, which is his statement: 'on its part', and the addition of this word excludes from the definition the indication of the word for the simple meaning, like the indication of the word 'point' for the end of the line, so the definition would be non-comprehensive. And it is answered: that 'completeness' does not imply composition like 'all', such that it would exclude the indication of the word for the simple meaning, because it is in opposition to 'deficiency', unlike 'all', for it is in opposition to 'some'. And it was said: that he mentioned it in opposition to 'part', and then it would imply composition, so it is preferable to delete it or replace it with 'ayn. His statement: 'the word' it is better that he uses an explanatory tool, because it is an interpretation of the agent's deputy, not that it is the agent's deputy as appears. And in it is an indication that the adjective or relative clause proceeded upon other than the one it is for, so it was necessary to manifest the pronoun, unless it is said: that he followed the way of one who says that it is not necessary to manifest if the proceeding is upon other than what is actually for it, but it is necessary in the adjective. His statement: 'upon the completeness of what it is placed for' meaning: upon the meaning which it is placed for in its completeness and its 'ayn, such that nothing of what the placer considered in opposition to it is excluded, and whether the word is polysemous or not, whether it is literal or metaphorical, so the indication of the polysemous word for each of its meanings is correspondence, and likewise the indication of the word for its metaphorical meaning, like the indication of 'lion' for the brave man. His statement: 'correspondence' meaning: it is called correspondence, i.e., corresponding indication. Al-Attar: His statement: 'upon the completeness of what it is placed for' the condition of completeness is not necessary in the definition, rather it is mentioned only to observe what good contrast requires with the second branch, and he did not use 'all' to indicate composition, (1) His statement: 'whether the word... etc.' so by 'placing' is meant what includes the real, which does not need a context as in literal meanings, and the interpretative, which needs a context as in metaphors, and personal placement as in some individuals, and generic placement as in derived terms and compounds, and whether the placement is general for general like placing universals, or general for specific like relative pronouns and demonstrative pronouns according to verification that they are universal in placement and particular in usage, contrary to the author, or specific for specific like placing personal proper nouns, and it is required in the polysemous the existence of a context so that its indication is not correspondence.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) by al-Dasuqi and al-Attar on the definition of mutābaqa (correspondence indication). The definition originally stated 'upon the completeness of what the word is placed for'. Al-Dasuqi first objects that adding the word 'tamām' (completeness) excludes simple concepts like 'point', because 'point' indicates the end of a line without composition. He defends the definition by noting that 'tamām' does not imply composition like 'jami'' (all). However, he then refutes this defense because 'tamām' is contrasted with 'juz'' (part), implying composition. He recommends deleting it or replacing it with 'ayn. Next, al-Dasuqi comments on the word 'al-lafẓ' (the word), suggesting that a grammatical explanatory tool is better, as it interprets the agent's deputy. He notes that the adjective should have a pronoun, but some scholars excuse it. Finally, al-Dasuqi explains the phrase 'upon the completeness of what it is placed for' as including full meaning, and notes that polysemous words and metaphors are included. Al-Attar adds that the condition of completeness is not necessary, but included for symmetry; the word 'jami'' was avoided because it implies composition. The footnote disambiguates 'waḍʿ' (placement) into real, interpretative, personal, and generic, and notes conditions for polysemy.

The Definition of Indication and the Necessity of a Relation
Author defines dalala and its necessary condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of dalala, identify the condition of a necessary relation (luzum), and explain why without it indication would be impossible.

Core Idea
Indication requires a necessary relation; otherwise everything would indicate everything.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational definition of dalala (indication) as presented in the Tadhheeb. The author insists that for something to function as an indicator, there must be a relation that compels the mind to transition from the indicator to the indicated. Without such a relation, the mind would have no reason to prefer one indicated thing over another, leading to contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of dalala
Find the sentence that begins with 'يلزم من العلم به العلم بشيء آخر' (knowledge of it necessitates knowledge of something else). That is the core definition.
2
Identify the condition of a relation
Notice the phrase 'إنَّما اشترط في دلالة شيءٍ على آخَرَ أنْ يكونَ بينَهُما علاقةٌ' (he only stipulated that there be a relation between them). This is the key condition.
3
Understand the reasoning
Read the justification: 'لولا ذلك; لدلَّ على جميع ما عداه' (otherwise it would indicate everything else). This is based on the principle that a preference without a preponderator is impossible.
This is a standard logical argument against arbitrary indication.
4
Apply the condition to an example
Consider a word and its meaning. Is there a relation (convention)? Yes. Consider a tree and a cloud? No natural relation? Then the tree cannot indicate the cloud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في تعريف الدَّلالاتِ الثَّلاثِ وأحكامها يلزمُ منَ العِلْم به العِلْمُ بشيءٍ آخر . الدسوقي واقتضاء الطَّبع في الطَّبيعية، والعلَّة في العقلية، وقوله: (يلزم ... إلخ)؛ خبر كون، وإنَّما اشترط في دلالة شيءٍ على آخَرَ أنْ يكونَ بينَهُما علاقةٌ تقتضي أن ينتقل منهُ إليه ؛ لأنَّهُ لولا ذلك؛ لدلَّ على جميع ما عداه؛ لأنَّ الانتقال إلى شيءٍ دونَ آخَر ؛ ترجيح من غيرِ مُرجّح . (قَوْلُهُ : يَلْزَمُ ) أي : بعد العِلم بتلك الحالة، وبعد العِلْمِ بالقرينة؛ ليشمل دلالة الألفاظ على معانيها المجازيَّة، والمراد اللُّزومُ الكُلّيُّ؛ أي: يلزم من العِلْمِ بِهِ في جميع أوقاتِ ذلكَ العِلْم ؛ العِلْمُ بشيءٍ آخر ، فَلَا ينفك عنه في وقتٍ مِن أَوقاتِهِ، والمراد بالعِلْم الأَوَّلِ ، والثَّاني الإدراك أعمُّ مِن أنْ يكونَ تصوريًا أو تصديقيًا يقينيا أو غيره، لكنَّ إنْ كانَ العِلْمُ بالشَّيء يفيدُ العِلْمَ التّصوريَّ؛ سُمِّيَ ذلكَ الشَّيءُ دالا وإنْ كانَ مُفيداً لِلعِلْم اليقيني ؛ سُمِّي ذلكَ الشَّيءُ دليلاً ، وإِنْ كانَ مُفيداً لِلظَّنِّ ؛ سُمّي ذلكَ الشَّيءُ دليلاً إقناعيًا وأمارة. واعلَمْ أَنَّ العِلْمَ غير اليقيني لا يُفيدُ عِلْماً يقينيا . (قَوْلُهُ : مِنَ الْعِلْمِ بِهِ) أي : بذلكَ الشَّيء، وقوله: (بشيء آخر) هو المدلول. العطار (قَوْلُهُ: يَلْزَمُ مِنَ الْعِلْمِ بِهِ قالَ عبد الحكيم: أي في الجملةِ كَمَا هو المقرَّرُ مِنْ أَنَّ الحُكْمَ إذا أُطلِقَ عن الجهة؛ يتبادرُ منه الإطلاق العام، أعني : بعدَ العِلْمِ بوجه الدَّلالةِ؛ أعني : الوضع أو اقتضاءَ الطَّبع ، أو العِليَّةَ والمعلولية، أو بالعلم بالقرينة ليشمل دلالةَ اللَّفْظ على المعنى المجازي، واللُّزومُ عِبَارَةٌ عَنِ امتناع الانفَكَاكِ بينَ الشَّيئين بأن لا يتخلَّلَ بينَهُما أمرُ آخَرُ؛ سواء كانَ في التَّحقُّقِ في وقتٍ واحدٍ كالإنسانِ والضَّحكِ، أو في وَقتَيْنِ مُستَعقِبَاً لهُ كالنَّظَرِ الصَّحيح والعِلْمِ بالنتيجة أو في العِلْمِ بأنْ يعلما معاً بأن يكون إحدُهُما متعقلاً قصداً والثَّاني تبعاً، وإلا ؛ فإحضار أمرَيْنِ بِالبال مُحالٌ كما في المتضايفين والمدلول المطابقي والتضمني والالتزامي، أو يكونُ العِلْمُ بأحدِهِمَا مُستعقِباً لِلعِلْمِ بالآخَرِ بِلَا فَضْلٍ ؛ كَمَا في الدليل والمعرَّفِ واللَّفْظِ والمعنى، والمراد بالعِلْمَ هَهُنا ؛ مُجرَّدُ الالتفاتِ والتَّوحِهِ كما صرَّحَ بِهِ قُدَّسَ سِرُّهُ في حواشِي المطالع، فَلَا يردُ أنَّه يلزم أن لا يكونَ لِلّفظ دلالة عند التكرار ؛ لامتناع عِلْمِ المعلومِ ا . هـ . هذه عبارتُهُ بِنَصِّها ، وبعضُ الحواشي بدَّدَ نظمَهَا وَمَحَا رَسَمَهَا .
Section: On the definition of the three indications and their rulings. There follows from knowledge of it knowledge of something else. (Al-Dasuqi: And natural requirement in natural things, and cause in intellectual things. His saying: 'there follows...' is the predicate of 'to be'. He only stipulated in the indication of a thing upon another that there be a relation between them that necessitates transitioning from it to it, because otherwise it would indicate everything else, since transitioning to one thing rather than another would be a preference without a preponderator. His saying: 'there follows' means after knowledge of that state and after knowledge of the context, to include the indication of words for their figurative meanings. The intended meaning is absolute concomitance, i.e., knowledge of it necessitates knowledge of something else at all times of that knowledge, so it is not separated from it at any time. The first knowledge and the second are perception, general whether conceptual or assentive, certain or otherwise. But if knowledge of the thing yields conceptual knowledge, that thing is called a 'dal' (indicator); if it yields certain knowledge, it is called a 'dalil' (proof); if it yields opinion, it is called a persuasive proof or sign. Know that non-certain knowledge does not yield certain knowledge. His saying: 'from knowledge of it' means of that thing. His saying: 'of something else' is the indicated. (Al-Attar: His saying: 'there follows from knowledge of it' said Abd al-Hakim: meaning in general, as established that when a judgment is absolute with respect to aspect, general application is understood, i.e., after knowledge of the mode of indication, i.e., convention or natural requirement or causality, or after knowledge of the context to include the indication of the word for the metaphorical meaning. Concomitance is an expression for the impossibility of separation between two things, such that no other thing intervenes between them, whether in actuality at one time, like man and laughter, or at two successive times like correct reasoning and knowledge of the result, or in knowledge such that they are known together, one being intentionally conceived and the other concomitantly, otherwise bringing two things to mind is impossible as in correlatives and the indicated by correspondence, inclusion, and implication, or that knowledge of one yields knowledge of the other without any added action, as in the proof, the definiendum, the word and the meaning. Knowledge here means mere attention and direction, as his blessed secret clarified in the glosses of al-Mutala', so it is not objected that the word would have no indication upon repetition due to the impossibility of knowing the known. End. This is his exact wording, and some glosses disrupted its organization and erased its drawing.)
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion of the concept of dalala (indication). It begins by stating the section heading: defining the three types of indication and their rulings. The core definition is that indication occurs when knowledge of one thing necessarily entails knowledge of something else. The commentator al-Dasuqi explains that this relation must be a natural requirement (in natural things) or causality (in intellectual things), and that without such a relation, everything would indicate everything else, which is absurd (preference without a preponderator). The phrase 'there follows' (yalzam) is qualified: it requires knowledge of the state and context to cover figurative meanings. The concomitance is universal, meaning at all times. The terms 'knowledge' are general perception, covering conceptual and assentive, certain or not. Then a key distinction is made: if the indicator yields conceptual knowledge, it is called 'dal' (indicator); if certain knowledge, 'dalil' (proof); if opinion, 'dalil iqna'i' or 'amara' (sign). Non-certain knowledge does not yield certain knowledge. Al-Attar then quotes Abd al-Hakim, who elaborates on the types of relation: convention, natural requirement, causality, and context. Concomitance is defined as impossibility of separation, with examples like man and laughter (at one time), correct reasoning and result (successive), and the relation between the definiendum and definition. The discussion clarifies that knowledge here is mere attention, not full comprehension, to avoid the objection that repetition would be impossible. The passage ends with a note that some glosses have distorted this text.

لزوم
علاقة

Checkpoint
According to the Tadhheeb, why must there be a relation between the indicator and the indicated?
A) Because the indicator must be a word and the indicated a meaning.
B) Because without a relation, the indicator would indicate everything, which is impossible due to preference without a preponderator.
C) Because the mind cannot know two things at once.
D) Because only God can create indications.

Key Takeaway
Indication is impossible without a necessary relation; otherwise the mind would have no reason to prefer one indicated over another.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Examine the Islamic legal principle that the general (al-'amm) indicates every individual (al-kull). What is the relation that makes this indication valid? (Hint: it is conventional.)
?
Identify an example from the Quran where a word indicates a meaning through a natural relation (tabi'iyya) rather than convention, if possible, and justify your answer.

Hadd and Rasm

The Three Types of Indication Based on Knowledge Type
Author distinguishes three types of indicators by the knowledge they produce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between dal, dalil, and amara based on the type of knowledge they yield (tasawwur, yaqin, zann).

Core Idea
Indicators are classified by the knowledge they yield: conceptual, certain, or opinion.

The author of the Tadhheeb makes a crucial distinction: the same relation of indication can produce different types of knowledge in the mind. Depending on whether the result is a concept, a certainty, or an opinion, the indicator receives a different name. This lesson unpacks that tripartite classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of knowledge mentioned
The text mentions 'العلم التصوري' (conceptual knowledge), 'العلم اليقيني' (certain knowledge), and 'الظن' (opinion). Note these.
2
Match each knowledge type to its indicator name
The text explicitly says: if the indicator yields conceptual knowledge -> it is called 'dal'; if certain knowledge -> 'dalil'; if opinion -> 'dalil iqna'i' or 'amara'. Memorize this mapping.
3
Understand the principle that non-certain knowledge cannot yield certainty
The text adds: 'العلم غير اليقيني لا يفيد علماً يقينياً' (non-certain knowledge does not yield certain knowledge). This is a logical principle about the multiplication of certainty.
This prevents using probabilistic evidence to prove certain truths.
4
Apply to a fiqhi example
Consider a hadith that is mutawatir (certain). It yields certain knowledge -> the hadith is a dalil. A single narrator hadith (khabar wahid) yields opinion -> it is an amara. A definition of a term yields conceptual knowledge -> it is a dal.

The Nature and Types of Luzum (Concomitance)
Author dissects the concept of luzum and its types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define luzum as impossibility of separation and identify its different types: simultaneous, successive, and knowledge-based.

Core Idea
Luzum is the impossibility of separation between two things, whether in existence or knowledge.

The commentary of Abd al-Hakim, quoted by al-Attar, provides a detailed analysis of the concept of luzum (concomitance). He defines it as the impossibility of separation between two things, and then divides it into various categories based on how the separation is prevented: in actuality at one time, at successive times, or in knowledge. This lesson explores these distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Define luzum from the text
Find the definition: 'اللُّزومُ عِبَارَةٌ عَنِ امتناع الانفَكَاكِ بينَ الشَّيئين' (concomitance is the impossibility of separation between two things). Memorize this.
2
Identify the first type: simultaneous actuality
Example given: 'الإنسان والضحك' (man and laughter). They are inseparable at the same time when a man is laughing.
This is a typical example of essential accident.
3
Identify the second type: successive actuality
Example: 'النَّظَرِ الصَّحيح والعِلْمِ بالنتيجة' (correct reasoning and knowledge of the result). The knowledge follows the reasoning in time.
Causal sequence.
4
Identify the third type: knowledge-based
Two subtypes: (a) known together, one being intentional and the other concomitant (e.g., correlatives like father and son); (b) knowledge of one yields knowledge of the other without extra effort (e.g., proof and conclusion).
5
Apply to an Islamic example
Consider the relation between 'iman' (faith) and 'amal' (action). In some theological views, they are inseparable in existence, i.e., luzum fi al-wujud. That would be simultaneous.

Source Text

فَصْلٌ: في تعريف الدَّلالاتِ الثَّلاثِ وأحكامها يلزمُ منَ العِلْم به العِلْمُ بشيءٍ آخر . الدسوقي واقتضاء الطَّبع في الطَّبيعية، والعلَّة في العقلية، وقوله: (يلزم ... إلخ)؛ خبر كون، وإنَّما اشترط في دلالة شيءٍ على آخَرَ أنْ يكونَ بينَهُما علاقةٌ تقتضي أن ينتقل منهُ إليه ؛ لأنَّهُ لولا ذلك؛ لدلَّ على جميع ما عداه؛ لأنَّ الانتقال إلى شيءٍ دونَ آخَر ؛ ترجيح من غيرِ مُرجّح . (قَوْلُهُ : يَلْزَمُ ) أي : بعد العِلم بتلك الحالة، وبعد العِلْمِ بالقرينة؛ ليشمل دلالة الألفاظ على معانيها المجازيَّة، والمراد اللُّزومُ الكُلّيُّ؛ أي: يلزم من العِلْمِ بِهِ في جميع أوقاتِ ذلكَ العِلْم ؛ العِلْمُ بشيءٍ آخر ، فَلَا ينفك عنه في وقتٍ مِن أَوقاتِهِ، والمراد بالعِلْم الأَوَّلِ ، والثَّاني الإدراك أعمُّ مِن أنْ يكونَ تصوريًا أو تصديقيًا يقينيا أو غيره، لكنَّ إنْ كانَ العِلْمُ بالشَّيء يفيدُ العِلْمَ التّصوريَّ؛ سُمِّيَ ذلكَ الشَّيءُ دالا وإنْ كانَ مُفيداً لِلعِلْم اليقيني ؛ سُمِّي ذلكَ الشَّيءُ دليلاً ، وإِنْ كانَ مُفيداً لِلظَّنِّ ؛ سُمّي ذلكَ الشَّيءُ دليلاً إقناعيًا وأمارة. واعلَمْ أَنَّ العِلْمَ غير اليقيني لا يُفيدُ عِلْماً يقينيا . (قَوْلُهُ : مِنَ الْعِلْمِ بِهِ) أي : بذلكَ الشَّيء، وقوله: (بشيء آخر) هو المدلول. العطار (قَوْلُهُ: يَلْزَمُ مِنَ الْعِلْمِ بِهِ قالَ عبد الحكيم: أي في الجملةِ كَمَا هو المقرَّرُ مِنْ أَنَّ الحُكْمَ إذا أُطلِقَ عن الجهة؛ يتبادرُ منه الإطلاق العام، أعني : بعدَ العِلْمِ بوجه الدَّلالةِ؛ أعني : الوضع أو اقتضاءَ الطَّبع ، أو العِليَّةَ والمعلولية، أو بالعلم بالقرينة ليشمل دلالةَ اللَّفْظ على المعنى المجازي، واللُّزومُ عِبَارَةٌ عَنِ امتناع الانفَكَاكِ بينَ الشَّيئين بأن لا يتخلَّلَ بينَهُما أمرُ آخَرُ؛ سواء كانَ في التَّحقُّقِ في وقتٍ واحدٍ كالإنسانِ والضَّحكِ، أو في وَقتَيْنِ مُستَعقِبَاً لهُ كالنَّظَرِ الصَّحيح والعِلْمِ بالنتيجة أو في العِلْمِ بأنْ يعلما معاً بأن يكون إحدُهُما متعقلاً قصداً والثَّاني تبعاً، وإلا ؛ فإحضار أمرَيْنِ بِالبال مُحالٌ كما في المتضايفين والمدلول المطابقي والتضمني والالتزامي، أو يكونُ العِلْمُ بأحدِهِمَا مُستعقِباً لِلعِلْمِ بالآخَرِ بِلَا فَضْلٍ ؛ كَمَا في الدليل والمعرَّفِ واللَّفْظِ والمعنى، والمراد بالعِلْمَ هَهُنا ؛ مُجرَّدُ الالتفاتِ والتَّوحِهِ كما صرَّحَ بِهِ قُدَّسَ سِرُّهُ في حواشِي المطالع، فَلَا يردُ أنَّه يلزم أن لا يكونَ لِلّفظ دلالة عند التكرار ؛ لامتناع عِلْمِ المعلومِ ا . هـ . هذه عبارتُهُ بِنَصِّها ، وبعضُ الحواشي بدَّدَ نظمَهَا وَمَحَا رَسَمَهَا .
Section: On the definition of the three indications and their rulings. There follows from knowledge of it knowledge of something else. (Al-Dasuqi: And natural requirement in natural things, and cause in intellectual things. His saying: 'there follows...' is the predicate of 'to be'. He only stipulated in the indication of a thing upon another that there be a relation between them that necessitates transitioning from it to it, because otherwise it would indicate everything else, since transitioning to one thing rather than another would be a preference without a preponderator. His saying: 'there follows' means after knowledge of that state and after knowledge of the context, to include the indication of words for their figurative meanings. The intended meaning is absolute concomitance, i.e., knowledge of it necessitates knowledge of something else at all times of that knowledge, so it is not separated from it at any time. The first knowledge and the second are perception, general whether conceptual or assentive, certain or otherwise. But if knowledge of the thing yields conceptual knowledge, that thing is called a 'dal' (indicator); if it yields certain knowledge, it is called a 'dalil' (proof); if it yields opinion, it is called a persuasive proof or sign. Know that non-certain knowledge does not yield certain knowledge. His saying: 'from knowledge of it' means of that thing. His saying: 'of something else' is the indicated. (Al-Attar: His saying: 'there follows from knowledge of it' said Abd al-Hakim: meaning in general, as established that when a judgment is absolute with respect to aspect, general application is understood, i.e., after knowledge of the mode of indication, i.e., convention or natural requirement or causality, or after knowledge of the context to include the indication of the word for the metaphorical meaning. Concomitance is an expression for the impossibility of separation between two things, such that no other thing intervenes between them, whether in actuality at one time, like man and laughter, or at two successive times like correct reasoning and knowledge of the result, or in knowledge such that they are known together, one being intentionally conceived and the other concomitantly, otherwise bringing two things to mind is impossible as in correlatives and the indicated by correspondence, inclusion, and implication, or that knowledge of one yields knowledge of the other without any added action, as in the proof, the definiendum, the word and the meaning. Knowledge here means mere attention and direction, as his blessed secret clarified in the glosses of al-Mutala', so it is not objected that the word would have no indication upon repetition due to the impossibility of knowing the known. End. This is his exact wording, and some glosses disrupted its organization and erased its drawing.)
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion of the concept of dalala (indication). It begins by stating the section heading: defining the three types of indication and their rulings. The core definition is that indication occurs when knowledge of one thing necessarily entails knowledge of something else. The commentator al-Dasuqi explains that this relation must be a natural requirement (in natural things) or causality (in intellectual things), and that without such a relation, everything would indicate everything else, which is absurd (preference without a preponderator). The phrase 'there follows' (yalzam) is qualified: it requires knowledge of the state and context to cover figurative meanings. The concomitance is universal, meaning at all times. The terms 'knowledge' are general perception, covering conceptual and assentive, certain or not. Then a key distinction is made: if the indicator yields conceptual knowledge, it is called 'dal' (indicator); if certain knowledge, 'dalil' (proof); if opinion, 'dalil iqna'i' or 'amara' (sign). Non-certain knowledge does not yield certain knowledge. Al-Attar then quotes Abd al-Hakim, who elaborates on the types of relation: convention, natural requirement, causality, and context. Concomitance is defined as impossibility of separation, with examples like man and laughter (at one time), correct reasoning and result (successive), and the relation between the definiendum and definition. The discussion clarifies that knowledge here is mere attention, not full comprehension, to avoid the objection that repetition would be impossible. The passage ends with a note that some glosses have distorted this text.

A) The necessity that a thing be known after another thing.
B) The impossibility of separation between two things, whether in existence or knowledge.
C) The relation between a proof and its conclusion.
D) The relation between two similar things.

Key Takeaway
Luzum is the impossibility of separation, which can be in actuality (simultaneous or successive) or in knowledge (co-known or sequential).

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
8 min
The Definition of Convention (Wad') and the Problem of 'Idha'
Author defines wad' (convention) as placing a thing in correspondence with another such that understanding the first leads to understanding the second.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definition of wad' and evaluate the logical appropriateness of the conditional particle 'idha' in that definition.

Core Idea
Wad' is placing a thing in correspondence with another such that understanding the first yields understanding the second.

This lesson examines the foundational definition of convention (wad') as presented in the text. The author carefully chooses words to ensure the definition is universal, not just for verbal signs. We will also see why the particle 'idha' (when) is problematic and why 'kullama' (whenever) better captures the required universal condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and the genus-differentia structure
Find the term being defined (wad') and note that the definition uses 'placing a thing' (jact al-shay') as a genus and 'in correspondence with another such that understanding the first leads to understanding the second' as the differentia.
The definition is a description (rasm) rather than a strict hadd.
2
Note the genericity of 'thing'
Observe that the definition says 'thing' (shay'), not 'word' (lafz). This indicates that wad' is absolute, covering all types of conventional relations, not just linguistic ones.
3
Analyze the condition for understanding
The definition requires that when the first (the placed thing) is understood, the second (the thing for which it is placed) is understood. This condition is essential for convention.
4
Critique the use of 'idha'
The particle 'idha' is normally used for occasional events. The commentator points out that it makes the proposition particular, implying that understanding the first sometimes leads to understanding the second. But convention requires universality. Hence, 'kullama' (whenever) is more appropriate.
This is a purely logical objection based on the semantics of conditional particles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْوَضْعُ : جَعْلُ الشَّيْءِ بإزاء آخَرَ ، بحيثُ إذا فُهِمَ الأَوَّل ؛ فُهِمَ الثَّاني. الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : وَالْوَضْعُ) أي : ومطلق الوضع؛ كان وضع لفظ أو وضع غيره، فهو تعريف لمطلق الوضع؛ لا لوضع اللفظ ؛ إذْ هو جعل اللفظ بإزاء المعنى، فقوله: (جعل الشَّيء)؛ أي : لفظاً كان أو غيره، وقوله : (بإزاء) أي : بمقابلة آخر، وهو الموضوع له . وقوله : (بحيث إذا فهم الأول)؛ أي: بحيث إذا أُدرك الأوَّلُ وهو الموضوع؛ أي : وعُلِمَ وضعُهُ لِلشَّيءِ الَّذي جُعِلَ بإزائه، وقوله: (فهم الثاني)؛ أي: وهو الموضوع له ، واعترض بأنَّ «إذا» للإهمال، فتكون القضيَّةُ معها في حكم الجزئية، فتقتضي أَنَّهُ إذا فُهِمَ الأَوَّلُ ؛ يُفْهَمُ الثَّاني تارةً، وتارةٌ لا يُفهم معَ أَنَّهُ لا بُدَّ في الوضع مِن فَهُم الثَّاني عند فهم الأوَّلِ في جميع الأحوال والأوقات، فكان المناسبُ إبدال إذا بـ «كُلَّما»؛ الَّتي هي من سور الإيجاب الكُلِّيِّ، فتأمل. (قَوْلُهُ : إِذَا فُهِمَ الْأَوَّلُ ؛ فُهِمَ الثَّانِي) أي : مع العِلْمِ بالوضع. العطار (قَوْلُهُ: وَالْوَضْعُ جَعْلُ الشَّيْءٍ) عدل عن اللَّفْظِ للعموم في سائر الأوضاع، وأمَّا وَضْعُ اللَّفظِ ؛ فإِنَّهُ يَنقَسِمُ إلى شَخصيّ ونَوعِيٌّ، وكُلُّ مِنهُما ينقسم إلى ثلاثة أقسامٍ؛ بيَّنَّاهَا غايةَ البيانِ في حواشِي شَرْحِ العِصَامِ على الوضعيَّةِ. (قَوْلُهُ : بِحَيْثُ إِذَا فُهِمَ الْأَوَّلُ ، فُهِمَ الثَّانِي) أي: عُلِمَ ، والعِلْمُ في الموضعَيْنِ بمعنى الالتفاتِ القصدي؛ إذْ لا ينتقلُ الدّهنُ مِن حضورِ اللَّفْظِ تبعاً إلى المعنى المطابقيّ، وَلَا مِنَ المعنَى المطابقي الحاصل تبعاً إلى المعنى الالتزامي؛ لأنَّ إحضار الملزومِ شَرْطٌ في الانتقال إلى اللَّازِمِ ، وَأَنَّ المراد باللُّزوم؛ الاستعقاب، فَلَا يردُ لزوم الالتفات إلى شَيئين في آن واحِدٍ، ولا يصح الجواب بأنَّه يجوز أن يكون الالتفات إلى أحدِهِما بالإحضار ؛ وإلى الآخَرِ بِالتَّبِعِ، وَمَا قِيْلَ إِنَّهُ يُشْكِلُ بما إذا كان المعنى مُلتفتاً إليه لأنَّه يلزم الالتفات إلى الملتفت إليه ؛ فَوَهُم، إذ لا يَشُكُ أحدٌ في أَنَّهُ كُلَّمَا اللفظ الموضوع لمعنى ؛ يلتفتُ الذَّهنُ إليه، والالتفاتُ الثَّاني غيرُ الأَوَّلِ، ا.هـ. عبد الحكيم، وبه تعلمُ مَا قِيْلَ هُنَا . شمع
And convention (wad') is: placing a thing in correspondence with another, such that when the first is understood, the second is understood. (Al-Dasuqi: His saying: 'and convention' means absolute convention, whether it is the convention of a word or something else. So it is a definition of absolute convention, not of the convention of a word, since the latter is placing a word in correspondence with a meaning. So his saying: 'placing the thing' means whether it is a word or something else. His saying: 'in correspondence with' means opposite to another, which is the thing for which it is placed. His saying: 'such that when the first is understood' means such that when the first—which is the placed thing—is perceived, and its placement for the thing in whose correspondence it was placed is known. His saying: 'the second is understood' means the thing for which it is placed. An objection is raised that 'idha' (when) is for [occasional] affirmation, making the proposition particular, implying that when the first is understood, the second is understood sometimes and sometimes not, whereas in convention, the second must be understood upon understanding the first in all cases and times. So it would be appropriate to replace 'idha' with 'kullama' (whenever), which is a quantifier of universal affirmation. Ponder. His saying: 'when the first is understood, the second is understood' means with knowledge of the convention. (Al-Attar: His saying: 'and convention is placing the thing' he turned away from 'word' to achieve generality for all conventions. As for the convention of a word, it divides into personal and generic, and each of them divides into three types, which we have explained thoroughly in the glosses on the commentary of al-‘Isam on al-Wad‘iyya. His saying: 'such that when the first is understood, the second is understood' means known, and knowledge in both places means intentional attention; because the mind does not transition from the presence of the word concomitantly to the meaning by correspondence, nor from the meaning by correspondence obtained concomitantly to the implicational meaning, because bringing the necessary is a condition for transitioning to the necessary. And that the intended meaning of 'concomitance' is 'following', so the objection of necessary attention to two things at one moment does not arise. Nor is the answer correct that it is permissible for attention to one of them to be by presentation and to the other by concomitance. And what is said that it is problematic when the meaning is attended to because it would necessitate attention to that which is attended to is a mistake, since no one doubts that whenever a word is placed for a meaning, the mind attends to it, and the second attention is other than the first. End of Abd al-Hakim's statement. By this you know what is said here. Sham‘)
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage defines wad' (convention) as a general concept. The core definition: placing a thing in correspondence with another such that understanding the first leads to understanding the second. Al-Dasuqi clarifies that this is absolute convention, not limited to words, so it covers any kind of conventional relation. The definition uses 'idha' (when), which an objector argues is a particle for occasional cases, making the proposition particular, whereas convention requires universal understanding (whenever the first is known, the second is understood). The commentator suggests replacing it with 'kullama' (whenever) to indicate universal affirmation. Al-Attar further explains that the definition deliberately uses 'thing' instead of 'word' for generality. He then discusses the types of verbal convention. The key technical point: the 'understanding' here means intentional attention, not full knowledge. This avoids the problem of attending to two things simultaneously, because the transition from the placed thing (word) to the meaning is successive, not simultaneous. Abd al-Hakim elaborates that the mind does not hold both at once; rather, one is attended to intentionally and the other follows. The passage ends with a note that this explanation resolves the difficulty.

Key Terms
وضع
إذَا
موضوع له

Checkpoint
Why does al-Dasuqi object to using 'idha' (when) in the definition of wad'?
A) Because 'idha' implies past tense, whereas wad' is a future act.
B) Because 'idha' is for occasional occurrence, but wad' requires universal understanding whenever the first is known.
C) Because 'idha' is a particle of condition, and the definition should be declarative.
D) Because 'idha' is ambiguous between time and condition.

Key Takeaway
The definition of wad' must be universal, so 'idha' (when) should be replaced with 'kullama' (whenever) to indicate that understanding the first always leads to understanding the second.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
